O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.  
O you, my dearest son, I have completed this book for you, which is the final one on the science of medicine together with its content, and I have concluded it through its explanations and clarifications.  

Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».  
And it has come to me in a vision that I should complete it for you with this treatise, which is part of manual work, namely "surgery."  

Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.  
And because manual work has been abandoned in our region and has been entirely neglected, the science has perished and been fragmented, with nothing remaining of it except the brief descriptions in the books of the ancients, which have become obsolete.  

Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.  
And from this have come error and vanity, intentions have been stifled, and the science has been estranged.  

Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;  
Now it seems to me that I want to revive it, together with the organization of this treatise, according to the method of exposition, clarification, and abbreviation;  

et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.  
and I will include the shapes of cautery instruments and other tools of the trade, along with explanations and preparations for their use, as is necessary.  

Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.  
And because no good masters of manual skills are found in our time, the art of medicine has been distanced.  

Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.  
And it is necessary for anyone who practices it to excel in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that he knows the structure of the limbs, their forms, connections, and separations, and has knowledge of the bones, nerves, ligaments, the number of veins, their movements and fixed positions, and the places of their origins.  

Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;  
And for this reason, Hippocrates says that the name without the deed is much, but with the work it is little;  

et meismement en l’art de main.  
and particularly in the art of manual work.  

Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;  
We tell you in the introduction to this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the previously mentioned matters must beware of falling into error and killing people;  

ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.  
just as I have often seen many of those who meddle in this science and proceed without knowledge and experience.  

Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;  
For I saw a foolish physician who cut open an abscess of scrofula on a woman's neck and severed the arteries of the neck;  

por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.  
causing so much blood to flow that the woman died in his hands.  

Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;  
And I saw another physician who attempted to remove a stone from an elderly man, and the stone was large;  

si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.  
and he removed with it a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.  

Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.  
And I had already been called to remove it, and I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and I knew well that if it were cut, he would die.  

Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;  
And I saw another physician who undertook the care of a duke from our land who had a broken leg and also a wound with the fracture;  

et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;  
and the physician, full of ignorance, pressed the fracture over the wound with splints very tightly and did not leave any drainage for the wound, and left it like that for a long time;  

et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;  
and he commanded that it should not be unbound;  

et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.  
and it remained in that state until the leg and foot were completely swollen and became ruined.  

Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;  
I was called to come to him, and I hastened to come and unbind the leg;  

et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.  
and when I unbound it, he was at peace and felt no pain.  

Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;  
But the corruption was already established in the limb, and I could not heal it;  

et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.  
and the corruption continued to spread through the limb until it was entirely lost.  

Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.  
And I saw another physician who punctured a cancerous abscess and then inflamed it through the malice of his intervention.  

Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.  
For a cancer, when it is pure from melancholic humor, must not be touched with iron unless it is in a place where one can entirely remove what is corrupted.  

Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:  
And for this reason, dearest son, you need to know that manual work is divided into two divisions:  

c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;  
namely, work where there is danger in many conditions;  

et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.  
and I will show in each part of this book where there is fear and danger.  

Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.  
For this reason, it is necessary for you to be cautious, so that foolish physicians cannot speak ill of you.  

Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;  
So take your tools with careful judgment, approach your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best method so that, by God's grace, you may bring healing and be praised.  

et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;  
And leave aside terrifying diseases of severe harm;  

et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.  
and put aside your tools when you are in doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you may pass from this world to the other in glory.  

Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:  
Galen says in some of his admonitions:  

«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.»  
"Do not take on the care of a bad disease, lest you be called a foolish physician."  

J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.  
I have divided this treatise into three chapters.  

Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;  
The first chapter is about cauterizations with fire and with sharp medicinal tools, and this chapter is organized from the head to the feet;  

et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.  
and about the shapes of the instruments, the cauterizing tools, and all that is necessary for the work.  

Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;  
The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and about cupping, wounds, the extraction of arrows, and similar matters;  

et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.  
and this chapter is organized along with the shapes of the instruments.  

Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;  
The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar matters;  

et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.  
and it is organized from the head to the feet, along with the shapes of the instruments.  

Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.  
Before we turn to the work, it is necessary that I speak of the qualities of benefit and harm in each temperament.  

Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;  
I say that the qualities of benefit and harm are the most extensive topic, the most subtle science, and the most hidden secret;  

et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;  
and many of the wise have spoken of this and have agreed upon it;  

et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.  
but their words suffice me little, as I fear their lengthiness.  

Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:  
I say that cauterization universally helps in all temperaments where there is matter, except for two temperaments:  

c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.  
namely, a hot temperament without matter, and a dry temperament without matter.  

En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;  
In a hot and dry temperament with matter, some debated and said that cauterization is of great help;  

et li autre dirent le contraire:  
and others said the opposite:  

que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.  
that cauterization is not useful for diseases that come from heat and dryness.  

Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;  
For the nature of fire is hot, and a hot disease must not be treated with heat, nor with dryness;  

et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.  
and the one who says the contrary states that cauterization is of great help for hot and dry diseases that occur in human bodies.  

Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.  
For when you compare the human body and its moisture to the temperament of fire, you find the body cold.  

Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.  
And I agree with this statement.  

Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.  
For I have found it to be true on some occasions through experience.  

Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;  
And yet, only those who have tested it and who know through long practice the chapter on cauterizations, the diversity of human temperaments, the conditions and causes of their diseases, their developments, and the duration of time, should engage in it;  

des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.  
as for other temperaments, we have no fear, especially in cold and moist diseases.  

Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.  
And all the physicians gathered and agreed upon cauterization.  

Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.  
And know, son, that cauterization using fire is among the secrets of healing and is of greater worth than cauterization with burning medicine.  

Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.  
For fire is simple and affects only the member that is burned, causing no harm to any other part.  

Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;  
Burning medicines spread from one member to another, worsening conditions and causing grievous afflictions to the member.  

et par aventure ocit lou malaide.  
And by chance, they may kill the patient.  

Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.  
Fire, due to its excellence and the nobility of its nature, does not do this unless there is excess.  

Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;  
And this I have discovered through experience and the long practice and study I have dedicated to the art, based on the truth of things.  

et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;  
And for this, I apologize for the length of my words, for I do not wish to deprive you of the secret contained in fire and the quality of its operation, how it drives away diseases of the body, as philosophers have demonstrated.  

or le recevez en vos pensees.  
Now receive it in your thoughts.  

Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.  
And know, son, that they agreed on the time when cauterizations should be done and chose springtime.  

Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;  
But I say that cauterization is appropriate at all times because the arising harm is alleviated with the help of cauterization.  

et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.  
And especially when the cauterization is for urgent and necessary pain that cannot wait for the time when greater harm may come to the member.  

Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;  
And do not ever think, dear son, as foolish doctors do.  

car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;  
For a disease cured by cauterization does not return.  

et il le dient ensi;  
And they say it thus;  

mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.  
But it is not as they think, because cauterization is only a medicine that alters the complexion, dries the humors that cause pain, and surpasses medicine due to the swiftness of its efficacy and the virtue of its operation and dominance.  

Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;  
And it is possible for the disease to return at times, depending on the patient's complexion, the location of the disease, and its strength.  

et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;  
And the excesses gather in him through the acquisition of food and similar things unless the cauterization is applied to a place with little excess and moisture, such as the cauterization of teeth for pain and similar issues, and such pain does not return.  

mais ce avient poc.  
But this happens rarely.  

Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;  
And many people do not understand why cauterization is called the last resort of medicine, and it is true;  

mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.  
But they do not believe that cauterization is valuable after medicine, and their understanding is false, for cauterization is the last resort of medicine because when we have applied various remedies to a disease and they fail, then we administer the cauterization, and it works.  

Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.  
Thus, it is clear that cauterization is the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention of foolish doctors.  

Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;  
The ancients said that cauterization with a gold instrument is better than with iron, and they said this only because of the quality of gold and the nobility of its nature.  

et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;  
And they said that the site of the cauterization does not rot, but this is not true, for I have tested it and found it true in some men.  

et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.  
And cauterization with gold is indeed superior to that with iron, as they said.  

Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;  
Yet, when you heat a gold instrument, you cannot tell when it is hot by the color of the gold, and it cools quickly.  

et s’on le chaufe trop;  
And if it is overheated,  

si font au feu;  
It becomes useless in the fire.  

et ensi i a assez d’empechement.  
Thus, there are many difficulties with it.  

Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.  
And for this reason, we use iron cauterization, which we have better adapted to our work.  

Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.  
Now I have arranged this chapter from head to foot so that the way may be easier to follow.  

dou cautere olivaire  
Of the olive cautery  

Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.  
This cautery is beneficial for moisture and cold on the brain, and there are two types made for a condition called "soda" and for the many humors that descend from the head to the eyes and ears, and for the multitude of dreams, toothache, sore throat, and especially for all diseases that arise from cold, such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar ailments.  

Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;  
The form of this cautery is such that the patient is purged with dissolving medicine cleansing the head for three or four nights, according to what the strength, age, and habits of the patient can endure.  

et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.  
Then shave the patient’s head.  

Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;  
Then have him sit cross-legged between your hands, and place his hands on his chest.  

aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;  
Next, place the base of your palm on the base of his nose between his two eyes.  

et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:  
And where your middle fingers land, mark with ink; then heat the cautery called "olivare," of which this is the procedure:  

Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;  
Place it on the spot marked with ink, pressing downward and tightening your hand little by little while turning.  

puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;  
Then quickly lift your hand and check the spot to see if you glimpse the bone slightly.  

et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;  
If you do not see it, repeat the cautery until you see the bone as I have described.  

aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;  
Next, take a little salt, place it in water, soak cotton in it, and place it on the spot, leaving it for three days.  

aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;  
Afterward, apply cotton moistened with butter.  

et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;  
Leave it on until the burn is healed.  

aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.  
Then treat the wound with the ointment called "tetrafarmaçon" until it is healed.  

Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;  
The ancients said that the longer the wound remains open, the more it purges.  

et por ce si aide mues.  
And thus it provides greater relief.  

Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.  
Some said that one must leave the cautery on until part of the bone is burned, and then scrape away what is burned and treat it.  

Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;  
Others said the cautery should be left in place and pressed so firmly that bone is removed as widely as a spindle-whorl used by women, so the humors are fully expelled.  

et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;  
The wound must be left open for a long time.  

aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.  
Then it must be treated and cauterized.  

Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;  
These two methods of cautery do not seem entirely good to me, except in some cases where the person shows clear signs of fear.  

et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;  
In many cases, it seems to me that I should avoid it.  

car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;  
For the head is weakened by the continuous natural evacuations, as we observe in other parts of the body.  

et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.  
Likewise, when the patient’s head is weak by nature, the first form of cautery is safer and more effective in my opinion, and I use it to work towards healing in such cases.  

de l’anciainne dolor dou chief  
Of the ancient pain in the head  

Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;  
When chronic pain occurs throughout the head and lasts a long time, the patient must use salves and pills called "cochie," along with head purgatives, oils, and plasters.  

et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.  
And if the cautery we previously described is applied and it does not help.  

Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;  
Take care if the patient’s head is of strong constitution and not too cold.  

adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.  
Then cauterize below the previous cautery a little, as we have described above.  

Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;  
Next, make a cautery on each horn of the head down to the bone, as we said earlier, and make one cautery at the spot called "vasselz."  

et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;  
This is the place where cupping glasses are applied.  

et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:  
Lighten your hand so that you do not reach the bone.  

li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;  
The patient feels much greater pain from this cautery than from others, and I will speak of it elsewhere.  

et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:  
The cauteries on the horns must be more delicate than those used to cauterize the center of the head, and this is the procedure:  

dou cautere dou chief  
Of the cautery of the head  

Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:  
When sudden pain comes to a part of the head and the disease extends to the eye, and the head has been cleansed with purifying medicines, and the other treatments I have mentioned in the division of diseases have been performed, and none of this helps:  

adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.  
Then perform cauterization in one of two ways, namely with sharp medicine or with iron.  

Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;  
The cautery with sharp medicine is done by taking a clove of garlic, removing the skin, and trimming it a little at both ends, then cutting the temple where the pain resides so that you can place the clove of garlic under the skin.  

et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;  
Once it is placed, bind it tightly and leave it for twelve hours.  

et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;  
Then unbind it, remove the clove of garlic, and leave the wound as it is for two or three days.  

puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.  
Next, apply cotton soaked in butter until the decay is expelled.  

Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;  
Afterward, treat it with ointment until it is healed.  

et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.  
If you wish, you can use some of the burning medicines I have described in the twelfth treatise on burning medicines.  

Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.  
The cautery with iron is performed as follows.  

Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:  
Heat the cautery iron, which has the following form:  

Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;  
It is called "clos" because its head is shaped like a nail with a slight curve and a small protrusion in the middle.  

et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;  
Place it on the painful spot, hold your hand steady, and lightly turn the iron until half the thickness of the flesh is burned.  

et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.  
Lift your hand to avoid burning the artery underneath, which would cause a heavy flow of blood.  

Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors;  
Afterward, soak cotton in saltwater and place it on the spot for three days.  

puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;  
Then apply cotton soaked in butter, and afterward treat the spot with ointment until it heals.  

et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.  
If you wish, cauterize this migraine with the cautery called "cultellare," using its point, but take care not to cut the artery in this migraine that is not chronic.  

de emigraine  
Of migraine  

Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;  
When you treat a migraine as previously described in the division of diseases, and it does not help, and you see that the cauteries with medicine and iron are insufficient, then you must heat the cautery called "cultellare" until it turns white.  

et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;  
Then mark beforehand on the painful spot a line half a finger long, and remove your hand once, pressing carefully so as not to cut the artery or reach the bone.  

et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;  
Beware of the jaw, which moves when eating, and of the nerve connected to it, to avoid causing paralysis or spasm in the patient; also beware of bleeding from the artery when it is cut, as this can cause great fear, especially for someone unfamiliar with this practice and not trained or experienced.  

et laisse l’uevre em mi voie;  
Leave the procedure incomplete.  

mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.  
But I will tell you how to stop the bleeding when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it is explained in this book.  

Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee;  
If you see that these cauteries do not suffice for the condition and the patient is resilient, cauterize the middle of the head as we have described, and treat the wound until it heals.  

et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz;  
If you wish, use the cautery described in the chapter on artery extraction, along with the cautery that has two blades.  

et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.  
This cautery is better and more effective than the other.  

de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor  
Of ear pain due to cold  

Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:  
When cold causes pain in the ear, and solutions and the other treatments described in the division have been applied without effect, then heat the cautery called "poins," which has the following form:  

Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche;  
Next, cauterize all around the affected ear, or both ears if the pain is in both, staying a little above the root of the ear after marking the spot with ink.  

et ait X poins entor chescune oreille;  
Make ten cauterizations around each ear.  

aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.  
Afterward, treat the spots until they heal.  

de la torture de la bouche  
Of the affliction of the mouth  

Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;  
The affliction that must be treated by cauterization is only that which arises from phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of diseases;  

et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.  
and cauterization must not be applied to conditions arising from dryness and spasms of the nerves.  

Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres:  
When you treat this type of affliction caused by phlegm through purges, evacuations of the head, and gargling, and this does not suffice, then it is necessary to cauterize the patient in three places:  

l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;  
one at the root of the ear, another slightly outside the temple, and the third at the meeting point of the two lips;  

et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce;  
and place the cauterization on the area that appears healthy, applying it near the top of the ear, slightly below the edge of the head, and another on the temple as long as a thumb;  

et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse;  
and leave the cauterization in place until half the depth of the flesh is burned;  

et c’est li forme dou cautere:  
and this is the shape of the cauterization:  

Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros;  
It resembles the small blade we described earlier, but it is slightly finer, and the knife must be a bit thicker;  

aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.  
afterward, treat the area as I have said before, until it is healed.  

Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres:  
When apoplexy is chronic and you treat it as we have said, and it does not improve, and the patient has no fever, then apply four cauterizations:  

II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac;  
two on the two corners of the head, one in the middle of the head, and one at the place called the "vessel" as we described earlier, and the last cauterization on the mouth of the stomach;  

et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.  
and let it be treated as we said earlier.  

de litargie  
Of lethargy  

A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil;  
For this illness, the patient must be given strong purges and pills to cleanse the brain;  

aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres;  
afterward, shave the patient’s entire head, and apply to the occiput the mustard plaster described in the treatise on plasters;  

et c’est li maniere dou cautere:  
and this is the method of cauterization:  

si lou fai si com j’ai dit.  
apply it as I have described.  

S’il est sanez ensi, boin est;  
If he is healed this way, it is good;  

et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros;  
and if he is not, make three cauterizations from the middle of the head descending to the neck, with a space between each cauterization of the width of a finger;  

et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu;  
treat it as with the others, and if you wish to add more and the patient is able to bear it, make one cauterization in the middle;  

et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;  
and if necessary, two more on the two corners, and treat it until he is healed;  

et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.  
and let the cauterizations be those called "olive-shaped," as I have said before.  

de la froidor dou chief  
Of coldness of the head  

Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit;  
The head must be cleansed with purges and the remedies we have mentioned earlier;  

aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col;  
afterward, shave the patient’s head, then cauterize the middle of the head, each corner, one at the back, and three on the spine of the neck;  

et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos;  
and if more is needed, and the body is moist and the patient is able to endure it, and the illness is severe, make four cauterizations on the spine of the back;  

et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main;  
and leave them until most of the flesh is burned, then lift your hand;  

aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.  
then treat it until he is healed, and let the cauterizations be those called "olive-shaped," as we have said before.  

de l’epilempsie  
Of epilepsy  

Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.  
The epileptic should not undergo cauterization except for those that are phlegmatic, and the brain must first be cleansed with purges and other remedies we described in the section when the patient is strong and able to take medicine.  

Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;  
And if it is a child who cannot endure it, make him use gargling and chewing to cleanse the brain frequently, along with good foods;  

aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne;  
afterward, shave the head in the middle, make one cauterization as we described earlier, and one cauterization on the vessel and on each corner;  

et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.  
and if the patient is strong and enduring, make cauterizations as I have described for one with paralysis and weakening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cauterizations be olive-shaped according to the method I have mentioned.  

Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:  
If the patient is a child, make a subtle cauterization according to this method:  

Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.  
When, due to melancholy, there are corrupt humors or moisture and thick phlegm, then cauterize with the type of cauterizations we have described for those with paralysis.  

Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.  
And if, due to melancholy, the humors are tending toward melancholy and the patient’s body is moist, then give him something to drink that will cleanse the brain, as was mentioned earlier in the division.  

Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide;  
Then shave the patient’s head;  

aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief;  
then make a well-formed linen ring, like a circle, and place it in the middle of the head;  

et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars;  
and let the patient sit cross-legged and be firmly held from all sides;  

aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien;  
then prepare the ointment, which consists of old sheep’s butter;  

et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir;  
and warm it over a gentle fire so that when it is applied, the fingers can withstand it;  

aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier;  
then pour it within the circle in the middle of the head and let it cool;  

et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.  
and do this for the patient once a week, along with other good treatments, until he is healed.  

Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.  
Or, if you wish, cauterize the area by making several points with the cauterization tool.  

Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument;  
This method of cauterization moistens the brain evenly;  

et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.  
and then apply cotton soaked in butter and chicken fat.  

de l’awe des eulz  
Of wateriness of the eyes  

Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.  
When wateriness first appears in the eyes, with the signs I mentioned in the division, begin by giving the patient something to drink to cleanse the head, keep him away from all moisture, and make him sweat or bathe several times on an empty stomach.  

Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I;  
Then instruct him to tilt his head back, cauterize the middle of the head, and make two cauterizations on the two temples if the flow of water affects both eyes together, or one if it affects only one eye;  

et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple;  
and with the cautery, cut all the veins and arteries beneath the flesh, and let the cauterizations be long, following the width of the temple;  

et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.  
and beware of excessive bleeding, and if you see too much blood flow, staunch it with whatever means you have.  

Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras;  
And I will teach you the precautions for artery extraction and incision, and how to stop it.  

et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.  
And sometimes cauterizations are made on the nape, beneath the two bones at the back.  

dou cors des larmes  
Of the flow of tears  

Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors;  
When the tears from the eyes are chronic and habitual and are upon the veins or beside the arteries visible externally on the head;  

et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz:  
and it is seen to be caused by cold, phlegmatic excesses, then perform the cauterization I mentioned at the start of the treatment for water descending to the eyes:  

I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os;  
one cauterization in the middle of the head, two on the two temples, and two on the nape beneath the two bones;  

et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.  
and if more is needed, cauterize carefully above the eyebrow with a small cauterization tool.  

dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz  
Of the flow of tears within the eyes  

Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies;  
When you treat it according to what we described in the division, and it does not help, then give the patient to drink for three nights consecutively;  

aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire;  
then shave his head and make a cauterization in the middle with an olive-shaped cauterization tool;  

et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous;  
and make two cauterizations with the tool called "clavilis" above the two eyebrows, slightly below the hairline;  

et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.  
and be careful not to cut the artery.  

Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:  
And this is the shape of the cauterization called "clavilis":  

Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».  
When the membrane of the eye is softened by illness and moisture, cauterize it with this cauterization tool called "olive-shaped."  

de coi ci est li forme:  
Of which this is the form:  

Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont;  
And if you wish, make two cauterizations above the two eyebrows as long as the eyebrows themselves;  

et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.  
and do not leave the tool in place longer than necessary to burn a third of the membrane, as I have described.  

dou poil qui point l’oil  
Of eyelashes that prick the eye  

Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:  
Sometimes it happens that the eyelashes are turned inward and prick the eye, and cauterizations are done in two ways:  

c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.  
either with fire or with a burning medicine.  

Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals;  
For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the eyelashes grow until they are long and even;  

et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.  
and if they prick him at their roots, restrain his eyes so that they do not move until they grow.  

Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain;  
When they appear and are equal, then place the patient in your care;  

aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz;  
then draw upon the eyelid skin a figure resembling the leaf of a myrtle, and the start of the mark should be near the eyelashes;  

puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:  
next, place cotton moistened with egg white and parsley mucilage on the eye, then heat the cautery of the following design:  

Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit;  
Afterwards, cauterize over the figure you have marked little by little many times, so that the tissue is burned at that spot;  

et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil;  
and the sign of success in the operation is that you see the eyelid drawn back and the eyelashes raised to the edge of the eye;  

adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;  
then lift your hand and leave it as is for three days, then place cotton moistened with butter until the burn is healed;  

aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.  
afterwards, treat it with ointment until it is healed.  

Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers;  
And if after this the eyelashes reappear, and the eyelid becomes soft, then redo the cauterization in the same place as before;  

et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.  
and if the eyelashes are disorderly, cauterize until the eyelid is restored to its natural position, is smooth, and the lashes no longer irritate the eye.  

Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte;  
The cautery of burning medicine is that you instruct the patient to let the lashes grow until they are long and even, then make a parchment shaped like a myrtle leaf;  

puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien;  
then take some French soap and quicklime, one measure of each, and grind them together well;  

et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz;  
and do this quickly so it does not cool, then spread it on the form you made in the shape of the myrtle leaf, and place it on the eyelid skin;  

et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi;  
and if the affliction is in one eye only, work on that one, and if in both, likewise;  

et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef;  
and place beneath the eye cotton moistened with egg white;  

et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.  
and the head of the patient should rest in your care, and place your index finger on the medicine, pressing lightly and adjusting each time the patient feels the sting of the medicine, for it will sting like fire.  

Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.  
When you have done this for a long time, remove the medicine with your finger.  

Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision;  
And when the stinging has subsided, wash the area with water and check if you see the eyelid raised as if by the effect of fire or an incision;  

et s’il est ensi, si est bien.  
and if it is so, then it is good.  

Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point;  
If not, apply the medicine again to the area where it has not worked, until your operation is even and the eyes are properly set;  

puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.  
then place cotton moistened with butter until the burned tissue has fallen away, and afterwards treat the area with ointment called "dyafenis" or others, until it is healed.  

Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.  
And it is necessary that you are very careful in your work, ensuring that none of the medicine falls into the eyes.  

Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant;  
And if the eyelid becomes soft afterward, and the lashes irritate the eye, then restart the application of medicine on the area of the softened eyelid, carefully, just as you did before;  

aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;  
then treat it until it is healed;  

et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:  
and this is the form of the myrtle leaf:  

Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;  
And know that men’s eyes vary in size, both large and small, and your adjustments should be made accordingly;  

et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.  
and let not the correct path be hidden from anyone dedicated to the study of this art.  

de la cure de fistule par cautere  
on the treatment of fistula with cautery  

Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.  
When you treat a fistula as we have discussed in the divisions of diseases, and your treatments are ineffective, then you must use cautery according to this method.  

Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;  
Instruct the patient to place their head in your care;  

et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;  
and have an assistant hold the patient’s head firmly in such a way that they do not move or turn their head;  

aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;  
afterward, place cotton moistened with egg white or parsley juice on the eye;  

aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:  
then heat the cautery, which is of this design:  

et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;  
it is shaped at the tip like the form of a vulture’s feather, together with the shaft being the cautery;  

se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;  
if you wish, it may be pointed from one end to the other, or if you prefer, shaped like a tent;  

mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.  
but in any case, the one with a tip is more useful for your work.  

Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;  
Afterward, press the fistula if it is open, draw out the pus, and dry it;  

et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;  
and if it is closed, open it and extract the filth;  

aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie;  
then apply the hot cautery strongly, holding your hand with the cautery above the nerve area near the eye to ensure your hand does not err;  

et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.  
and place the cautery into the fatty tissue of the eye and destroy it.  

Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.  
If you reach the bone with the initial cautery, it will be good.  

Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;  
If not, redo the cautery again, or even more if necessary, and leave it for three days;  

aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers;  
then place cotton moistened with butter on it, and treat it with drying ointment until it is healed; if forty days pass without healing, apply a corrosive sharp medicine until the bone is exposed;  

et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.  
and follow the instructions as outlined in its proper section.  

Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.  
And there is a method of cauterizing a fistula described by some of the ancients.  

Entens a fistule, et fens le leu;  
Address the fistula and make an incision in the area;  

aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:  
then insert into the incision a fine camahan of the following design:  

et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc;  
it is made to the size of one measure of lead;  

et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;  
hold the camahan firmly with your hand, and ensure the patient does not move at all, lest the melted lead run into their eye;  

et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe:  
and it is necessary to place cotton moistened with egg white or water over the patient’s eye;  

li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.  
the lead burns the fistula area and heals it with remarkable efficacy.  

Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.  
And if the fistula is healed by the cautery as we described, it is good.  

Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.  
If not, it is necessary to make perforations in the nerve and guide the fistula back to the nerve's body as required in its proper place.  

Des crevaices en levres  
On cracks in the lips  

Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.  
Cracks often appear on the lips, called "poil," especially on the lips of children.  

Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:  
When you treat these cracks as described in the divisions, and the treatment does not work, then heat a small knife-shaped cautery of the following design:  

Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font;  
And quickly apply it to these cracks until it reaches their base;  

aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.  
then treat the area with wax ointment until it is healed.  

De l’aposteme de la goule  
On abscesses of the throat  

Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;  
When an abscess occurs at the root of the throat, the uvula, the palate, or the roots of the teeth, it becomes decayed, ruptured, chronic, and turns into a fistula;  

et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie:  
and you treat it as we described in the divisions, but it does not work:  

adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;  
then it is necessary for you to use a cautery matching the size of the fistula;  

aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu;  
then apply it to the opening or perforation of the fistula, and hold your hand until the hot iron reaches its base and farthest point;  

et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;  
do this once or twice, then treat it as we have explained in the treatments until it is healed;  

et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin;  
and if it heals in this way, it is good;  

et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.  
and if not, it is necessary to uncover the area and remove the corrupted bone as described in its section.  

Dou movement des dens  
On loose teeth  

Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;  
When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth become loose, and treating them with medicines does not work, then place the patient’s head in your care;  

aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent;  
then heat the cautery, whose shape is as follows, in such a way that you place a tube over the tooth;  

et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;  
and insert the hot cautery into the tube quickly, and hold it until the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth;  

aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit;  
then lift your hand and reapply the cautery as needed;  

aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.  
afterward, have the patient fill their mouth with salted water, hold it for an hour, and spit it out.  

Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.  
And in this way, the tooth that was loose is stabilized, the softened gums are tightened, and the corrupted moisture is dried.  

de la dolor des dens  
On the pain of teeth  

Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:  
When tooth pain comes from cold, or there is coldness or humidity, and medical treatments are ineffective, then cauterization is needed in two ways:  

et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.  
Cauterization with butter and cauterization with fire.  

Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;  
Cauterization with butter is such that you take cow’s butter and melt it in an iron or bronze spoon;  

aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;  
then take cotton, wrap it around the tip of a probe, soak it in the boiling butter, and quickly place it on the aching tooth, holding it there until it cools;  

et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.  
and do this often until its effect reaches the root of the tooth, and if you wish, soak wool and cotton in cold butter, place it on the aching tooth, and apply hot iron until the heat reaches the root of the tooth.  

Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;  
Cauterization with fire is such that you take an iron or bronze rod, making it thick enough so that the fire does not reach the patient's mouth;  

aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;  
then heat the cauterizing rod, whose shape will be described later, and place it on the tooth, holding your hand until the rod cools;  

fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.  
do this often, for the pain will be removed that very day or the next.  

Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;  
And the patient should fill their mouth with good butter during the application of the cautery, then spit it out afterward;  

et c’est li forme dou cautere:  
And this is the method of cauterization:  

Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir;  
And make the cautery on whatever part you wish, according to your ability;  

et c’est li forme de la caine:  
And this is the shape of the rod:  

des scrophules  
On scrofula  

Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie;  
When scrofula is caused by phlegm and cold moisture, and does not respond to digestion with medicines, then heat the head of the cauterizer, whose shape will be described later, and make two openings for the fumes to escape from the other side of the cautery;  

et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume;  
and place the heated cauterizer on the abscess once or twice as needed, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess;  

et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors;  
and if the abscess is small, apply the cauterizer according to the size of the abscess, and leave it as is for three days;  

et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee;  
and apply cotton soaked in butter until the burn is removed;  

aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.  
afterward, treat the area with ointments and dressings until it is healed.  

Li forme de la cainne:  
The shape of the rod:  

Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives;  
When moisture overcomes the passages of the lungs, especially when it comes from a cold complexion, then the patient must first be treated with purgative medicines;  

aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.  
then make a cautery at the root of the throat, and take care not to go as far as the throat, and burn only a little of the flesh.  

Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant;  
Then make another cautery at the junction of the neck and the top of the spine, using the cauterizer called “clavicle,” whose shape we described earlier;  

et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.  
and treat the area as we described earlier until it is healed.  

de la toust  
On coughs  

Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai .II cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis;  
When coughs and lung diseases are caused by cold moisture, and the patient has no fever or dryness, and the illness is chronic, make two cauteries on the chest in empty spaces;  

et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles;  
and another cautery in the middle of the chest between the two breasts;  

et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.  
and use the cauterizer called “clavicle” according to the shape described earlier.  

Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles;  
And if you wish, make a cautery with a pricking action using the cauterizer called “point,” whose shape was described earlier in the section on ear diseases;  

et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.  
and make as many as thirty pricks, or around that number.  

Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:  
Afterward, treat the area as described earlier, and use the cautery with three prongs in this manner:  

Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.  
And thus the cautery is lighter because you perform three at once.  

de la dislocation de l’ajutoire  
On dislocation of the jaw  

Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.  
When the head of the jaw is dislocated due to moisture, and it is put back in place but does not stay, instead dislocating again with small movements, as we have observed, then it is necessary first to reduce the dislocation.  

Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit;  
Afterward, let the patient lie on their back and on their side;  

aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre;  
then lift the flesh within the affected joint with the fingers of your left hand;  

et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:  
and if the joint is dislocated inwardly, then heat the cauterizer with two prongs, whose form is described here:  

et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres;  
and cauterize the flesh so that it penetrates to the ribs, and this creates the effect of the cautery combined with four cauteries;  

et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres;  
and thus cauterization is done with the cauterizer that has three prongs, so that the figure of the cauterization consists of six cauteries;  

et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:  
and the prongs are as fine as a probe, and this is the shape of the cauterizer with three prongs:  

Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.  
And sometimes an additional prong is added, resulting in eight cauteries.  

Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil;  
Afterward, apply crushed leeks mixed with salt to the cauterized area;  

aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.  
then let the patient rest, and do not move the limb for a long time until it is well strengthened.  

Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.  
And if it is dislocated above, which rarely happens, then make a cautery on the thick part with the “clavicle” cauterizer, or many pricking cauteries.  

Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.  
For the joint is restored, the moisture is removed, and the patient is healed.  

Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.  
When coldness and much moisture affect the stomach to the point that it alters its natural condition, and catarrh increases there, and the usual methods of treatment are ineffective, then the patient must lie on their back and stretch out their legs and arms.  

De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture;  
After that, make three cauteries: one beneath the hollow of the breastbone, the size of a finger, with the “clavicle” cauterizer, and two on the sides, so that the shape of the cauteries forms a triangle, leaving enough space between them that they do not connect when they discharge pus;  

et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:  
and make the cauteries deep enough to affect both sides of the heart, and the shape of the cauteries should follow this form without addition:  

Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme;  
And if you wish, cauterize the middle of the stomach with a large cauterizer in this shape;  

et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche;  
and for those who fear this cautery, cauterize with pricks and bleed the stomach at a single point, according to the size you prefer on the side;  

puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».  
then cauterize it with the cauterizer called “point.”  

Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.  
Afterward, treat the area as we have described earlier, until it is healed.  

Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez;  
When cold and moisture and thick windiness affect the liver, disrupting its natural condition due to excesses;  

et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil;  
and the patient has been treated according to the methods we have described in sections, but to no avail, then the patient must lie on their flank;  

et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient;  
and mark three cauteries in this shape, figure, and size over the liver, outside the hypochondrium, where the rib cage begins;  

et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi;  
and leave a space between each cautery the width of a finger;  

et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere;  
and make the cauteries along the length of the body, pressing lightly with the cauterizer;  

et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez;  
and burn only half the flesh, and let the patient stand upright;  

et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais;  
and if they cannot stand, then let them lie down, stretch their legs, and raise their arms;  

et c’est li forme:  
and this is the method:  

Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors;  
And if you wish, cauterize these areas with the knife cauterizer, if you are skilled and wise in the art, and take care not to burn all the flesh, for that would dry out the whole body;  

et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.  
and ensure it does not reach the boiling point, for the flesh is very delicate in that area, and this you should know for certain.  

Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile:  
When there is an abscess on the liver, and you wish to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane:  

s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort;  
if it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain, but not too intense;  

et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.  
and if it is in the membrane, the pain is excruciating.  

Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste;  
And then, when this treatment is described by the physicians, the patient must lie on their back;  

et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:  
and then bleed the area where the abscess is located, and heat the cauterizer that resembles a rod, whose form is described here:  

Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers;  
And cauterize one cautery until the core is burned, and it reaches the syphac, until all the corruption is expelled.  

aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez;  
Afterward, treat it according to the method of draining until it is healed.  

et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.  
And no one should use this cautery except one who has long studied the art of medicine and has treated such illnesses with his hands many times.  

Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.  
Then he may proceed boldly, yet it seems to me that often it is better to avoid it.  

dou cautere de pleuresin  
Of the cautery for pleuresy  

Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere:  
The ancients said that for pleurisy, cauteries should be made with roots of aristolochia, and in this manner:  

pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois;  
Take a long root of aristolochia, the largest you can find, and it should be dry, as thick and as long as your fingers.  

et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe;  
Dip its marrow in oil, set it in the fire, and apply one cautery between the hollow and the neck, and two small cauteries slightly descending on the part below the chin.
