and the chamber where the medicine is placed should be made from an animal bladder or parchment, and it should be pierced all around with small holes, and there should be one finger's width between each hole; then insert a strong thread, twisted tenfold or so around, and assemble the chamber as one does a leather bottle.  

et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize;  
and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument in front with a strong thread, then administer the enema.  

et c’est li forme dou cercle:  
And this is the shape of the circular attachment:  

Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;  
And the medicine should be neither too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the enema instrument with oil, egg white, or something similar, then insert it gently;  

puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet;  
then the practitioner squeezes it with both hands together until it is completely empty, then withdraws the enema instrument, and the patient raises their legs to the wall, and if the medicine wants to come out, hold it in as long as possible;  

et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.  
and if they sleep with it overnight, it is of greater benefit.  

Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.  
And if you administer it for the illness of diarrhea, and the medicine comes out too quickly, repeat it until they are healed.  

Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant;  
And if there are hemorrhoids in the anus, or an abscess, the enema should be as delicate as for a child;  

et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:  
and this is the form of the delicate enema, on which the skin is tightened:  

des plaies  
Of wounds  

Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies;  
We have already spoken in the division about the treatment of wounds;  

or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.  
now we shall discuss the treatments by hands and medicines, as a conclusion.  

Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.  
I say that wounds differ according to what causes them, the places where they are made, and what they are made by.  

Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;  
The things by which wounds are made include the throwing of stones, the cuts of swords and knives, or of spears or wooden shafts or plates, or similar things;  

ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;  
or wounds that occur in specific places on the body, such as wounds that fall on the neck, or on the head, or the chest, or the belly, or the liver, and similar parts;  

et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.  
and I shall tell you the treatment for each type of wound, and begin with simple wounds of the head, as the detailed explanations will come in their chapters.  

Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut:  
I say that when a simple wound appears on the head, and the bone is not broken, take note whether it is caused by the throwing of a stone or similar things, and the skin is still torn and the wound is large, and you suspect the development of a hot abscess:  

si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;  
then immediately let blood from the cephalic vein, especially if little blood comes from the wound, and the bloodletting should be on the side opposite to the injured part;  

et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.  
and the patient should avoid excess wine and heavy foods.  

Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;  
And if he does not wish to bleed, let his food be reduced, and let him drink no wine, nor consume any meat.  

et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;  
and place on the wound, if hot abscesses appear there, cotton moistened only in rose oil, or in styptic wine;  

et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;  
and if there is no hot abscess, then place on the wound, if it is fresh with its blood and has not been altered by the air, a powder, which I will describe a little further on;  

et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.  
and if the burn has altered it, then apply certain ointments until it is healed.  

Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.  
And if the wound is large, as from a sword slash or similar, and the edges cannot be brought together with tents, then join them with sutures, as I will describe for wounds of the abdomen, by stitching.  

Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope;  
If the wound exposes the bone, and it hangs and is attached by only a little, then cut it off;  

puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.  
then treat the wound with medicine, and restore firm flesh in place of skin, and command the patient to eat hearty foods, such as heads and cooked wheat, as well as poultry and similar things.  

Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;  
And if you find rot in the flesh, and it does not affect the bone, then cut away all the rot and throw it away, then treat it;  

et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;  
and if there is an artery or vein in the wound, from which blood flows and cannot be stopped by medicines, then locate the artery, and if you find it loose, tie it with a thread;  

et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.  
and if that does not work, then cauterize it.  

Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere:  
And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is easy:  

et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.  
and it is that you place in it this powder which seals before the burn has altered it.  

Et li maniere de la poudre si est:  
And the manner of the powder is as follows:  

pren encens une partie;  
take one part incense;  

sanc de dragon II parties;  
two parts dragon’s blood;  

chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;  
three parts quicklime, and grind it finely, and fill the wound with it, and compress it firmly, so that it adheres well and unites with its blood;  

et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle;  
and then bind it well, and leave it without unbinding, unless it swells;  

car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.  
for the medicine should not be removed until it is healed.  

Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.  
And sometimes this is done with only quicklime, when incense or dragon’s blood is not available, as long as the burn has not altered the wound.  

Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;  
And if the burn has altered the wound, especially in summer, then one does not place this powder there;  

mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;  
but applies some digestive ointments, or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, until it expels pus;  

puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  
then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.  

Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;  
And if a fragment of bone accompanies the wound, and it is small, then extract it with fine pincers;  

et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.  
and I will tell you further on about fractures of the skull.  

de la plaie dou col  
Of the wound to the neck  

Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.  
If a wound occurs on the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and one on the head, except if the nerve or artery in the neck is cut.  

Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;  
If it is the nerve, there is no other remedy than to abandon treatment, and not to place anything constricting there, for it harms the nerves and causes them to contract;  

et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;  
and place nothing cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their connection is with the brain, which is the highest organ;  

mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.  
but the medicine should be mild, such as warm herbs washed in sweet water and mixed with rose oil, or cucumbers washed similarly in sweet water, and other mineral substances prepared in this way, and moist ointments.  

Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.  
And if the wound is large, then sew it and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.  

Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;  
And if the wounds are deep and hollow and full of pus, then puncture it at a lower point;  

et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;  
and if the artery is cut, and blood flows from it, then uncover it, tie it, and cauterize it if necessary;  

et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;  
and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the throat, and the passage through which food goes is preserved, then sew the throat over the trachea, and do not touch the trachea but restore it to its natural shape;  

et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;  
then bind it appropriately, and leave it for some days, then treat it with drying ointments until it is healed;  

et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;  
and if the wound has left an impression on the bone, then examine it;  

et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue;  
and if there are pieces of bone, extract them all if you can, and those you cannot remove, leave them until the wound decays, and the issue becomes loosened and eased;  

et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.  
and if the wound is fresh, then sprinkle the powder I mentioned over it.  

Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.  
And if there is bone in the wound and a fistula, treat it as I described in its chapter.  

de la plaie de lance ou de coutel  
Of the wound from a lance or knife  

Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne:  
If it is a blow from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, then observe whether air escapes from the wound when the patient breathes:  

saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;  
then know that the wound is mortal;  

et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;  
and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with its blood, do not place the powder on it in the first hour, nor bind it, for the blood might not settle at the bottom, and it could return to the heart and kill the patient;  

mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor;  
but apply an attractive ointment, and bind it twice a day;  

et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors;  
and if you do not have ointment, place old cotton in the wound to absorb the moisture, and have the patient lie on the wound for three days, or four, or more;  

si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne;  
so that spasm, trembling of the heart, or difficulty breathing will not occur;  

et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.  
and when you see good progress, then know that the wound is safe.  

Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;  
Then treat it with tents and other remedies until it is healed;  

et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule;  
and if it cannot heal, then operate, knowing that there is a fistula;  

si la cure si com on doit.  
then treat it as it should be.  

Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;  
And if the wound is from an incision by a sword or knife, and it is simple, either on the chest or the back, treat it as I described above;  

s’elle est grans, de cousture;  
if it is large, with sutures;  

et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;  
if it is small, with powder, and if it has pressed into the bone and broken pieces, then examine the wound and remove them if they are detached;  

et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;  
and if they are not detached, then let the wound rot, so that the extraction becomes easier;  

et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.  
and for other wounds on other parts of the body, the treatment is as we have described.  

dou derrompement dou ventre  
Of the rupture of the abdomen  

Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;  
The ruptures of the abdomen are large, medium, and small;  

de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;  
from the large wound sometimes the intestines, or the nerves of the intestines, protrude, through which their reentry;  

et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;  
and the suturing is more difficult, and sometimes the small wound is worse than the large one, because it is more difficult to replace the intestines unless they are returned little by little;  

por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.  
because the intestines swell as soon as they feel the cold, making reentry more difficult, and for this reason the medium wound is better, as it allows the intestines to be returned to their place more easily than the other two.  

Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:  
And know that the ruptures of the abdomen occur in four ways:  

les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;  
two common sutures are used in suturing the abdomen, and the sutures of other wounds of the body and two other specific sutures are shared with other wounds;  

et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.  
and yet they are more appropriate for the suturing of the abdomen, and I will name and explain each one.  

Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:  
I say that when the wound is small, and some part of the intestine protrudes, it is difficult to replace, and this happens in one of two ways:  

ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.  
either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen from the cold.  

Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:  
And when it is cold, warm it in this way:  

moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;  
moisten a sponge or a soft cloth in warm water only, or boil water with hyssop, cypress, and spike, and bathe the intestine until the swelling is reduced;  

et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.  
and sometimes use astringent wine, which is better than plain water for reducing swelling.  

Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;  
And when you see the swelling subside, moisten the intestine with water in which marshmallow and mallow have been boiled, for this eases its reentry little by little;  

et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;  
and if it cannot reenter, slightly enlarge the wound with the instrument used for cutting hemorrhoids;  

et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;  
and the first treatment is better than cutting, as one must not cut unless there is great necessity;  

et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:  
and this is the instrument for enlarging it:  

si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:  
it cuts inside in the curve but not outside, and here is the shape:  

Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.  
And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines protrude, return them to their proper place in their natural form if you are able, for this is much better.  

Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;  
When the wound is large and it is in the lower part of the abdomen, you must have the patient lie on his back and raise his legs higher than his head;  

et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;  
and if it is in the lower part of the abdomen, raise the head and chest higher than the lower parts, and likewise if the rupture of the abdomen is in one of the two sides, ensure that the injured part is higher than the other;  

et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.  
and thus you must manage what I have described for large and medium wounds.  

Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;  
For small wounds, apply what is prepared, then have in your hands a compassionate assistant who holds the entire rupture with his hand and joins the lips.  

et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;  
And this is the common method of suturing: take one or more needles, depending on the size of the wound, then leave a finger's breadth from the edge of the wound and insert a needle with a strong thread.  

et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;  
Pierce through the two edges of the skin along with the two edges of the fascia, which lies under the skin, so that you pierce it on that side and join the two edges of the fascia together with the four layers.  

puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;  
Then wrap a double thread around the needle on both sides, then join the two edges of the wound evenly, and leave a finger’s breadth again before inserting another needle.  

puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;  
Then tie the thread as you did with the first needle, and continue doing this according to the need for needles until the entire wound is closed.  

et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:  
And the needles should be of medium size, neither too fine nor too thick, because fine needles cut through all the flesh, and overly thick ones cannot enter properly.  

por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;  
Thus, they must be medium.  

et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;  
And the needles must not penetrate too far outside the flesh and skin, as they would cut and reopen the wound before it can heal.  

et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;  
Then cut off the ends of the needles so they do not injure the patient while sleeping, and place plugs or cloths at the ends of the needles to hold them in place, and leave them until the wound is healed.  

et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.  
And this method of suturing with needles is more suitable for small wounds, as one or two needles suffice.  

Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;  
The second suture method is common and involves joining the two edges of the skin and the two edges of the fascia together with one needle threaded with a medium-strong thread.  

et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;  
And when you have pierced all four layers together, bring the needle back to the side where you started, in the same way one sews cloth.  

et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;  
And leave a space between each stitch equivalent to the thickness of a small finger.  

ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.  
This suture is well-known, and I once sutured a wound on a man’s abdomen who had been injured by a knife. The wound was more than a palm’s width in size, and about two palms of intestines were protruding, with the wound located in the middle of the abdomen.  

Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.  
I returned the intestines to their place after they had been exposed for twenty-four hours, and the wound healed within fifteen days, and I treated him, and he recovered.  

Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;  
The physicians had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle.  

et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;  
And I did not treat him with ointments, as I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicines.  

et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.  
I simply placed old cotton on the wound twice a day and washed it with honey water until he was healed.  

Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:  
Now I will tell you about the two specific suturing methods:  

pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;  
Take the needle and insert it from the outer part to the inner part.  

quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;  
When it has pierced the fascia straight through, leave the edge of the fascia where you inserted the needle and pierce it again from the inner part to the outer part on the other side.  

et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.  
The idea of this suture is that you sew as tanners do with skins, leaving the fascia on one side once and picking it up on the other until the suture is fully completed.  

Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:  
The second method of suturing, which Galen properly describes, is as some do, joining the two parts naturally and applying one edge of the fascia to the other in this manner:  

fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;  
Insert a needle into the nearby edge of the wound and pierce that spot only, leaving the two edges of the fascia.  

puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;  
Then turn the needle and pierce it from the outer part to the inner part at the two edges of the fascia.  

puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;  
Then pierce both from the outer part to the inner part, at two other edges of the wound on the opposite side.  

et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.  
And this is the best and most common method of suturing.  

Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;  
Galen said this statement, and some attest to it, that one must sew the belly with two needles, each having a thread;  

et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;  
and one must insert one needle on one side and the other on the opposite side, in the manner of those who sew straps;  

et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.  
and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, the stitching is more difficult than in other places of the belly.  

Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:  
The treatment of the wound is the same as the treatment of other wounds:  

et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;  
and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, before the inflammation has altered it, you must replace the intestine and sew it;  

puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;  
then apply the powder that generates flesh, and if the inflammation has altered it, apply any available ointment until the wound suppurates;  

et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;  
and let the threads fall off, and let the scar and the healing unite;  

puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;  
then treat the wound as with others, until it is healed;  

et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.  
and if you lack medicines, then as soon as it begins to discharge pus, apply old cotton and change it twice a day until it is healed.  

Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;  
For you have no need of other medicines in many cases when the wounds are simple;  

et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;  
and if you fear that the wound might cause complications to the principal members, you must soak light wool in moderately heated oil or rose oil and apply it around the groins and under the armpits;  

et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;  
and if there is pain or putrefaction in the bowels, which often happens, administer an enema of warm black wine, especially if the putrefaction reaches the intestine;  

et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.  
and pierce it inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.  

Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.  
The intestine called "jejunum" cannot heal when it is injured, and this is due to the density of the veins there, the delicacy of the whole body, and its proximity in nature to the nerves.  

Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;  
And if the mesentery protrudes from the wound, replace it as you would the intestine, as long as it is fresh;  

et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;  
and if it is old and has turned green or black, you must tie off the blackened area to prevent blood flow there, as there are veins and arteries;  

puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.  
then cut what lies between the ligatures, and let the two ends hang down from below the wound to the outside to facilitate the removal when the mesentery falls, and the wound suppurates.  

de la routure dou boueil  
Of the rupture of the bowel  

Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;  
When the intestine is round and the wound is small, it can be repaired in some men, as I saw a man who was wounded in the belly by a lance;  

et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;  
and the wound was to the right of the stomach, and it became old and turned into a fistula, and excretions and gas escaped from it;  

je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.  
I treated it as best I could and persisted in my efforts until it was healed and the place closed up.  

Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;  
And when I saw it close, I feared that the patient might have pain in his belly;  

et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;  
but he had no pain and remained in better health, eating and drinking.  

et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:  
And some practitioners said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be bound in this way:  

pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;  
Take clamps with large heads, then bring together the lips of the wound, and when the clamp opens its jaws, place it on the two lips so that it pinches them shut;  

et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;  
then cut off the head of the clamp, and it holds so that it cannot come loose, then place another clamp in the same way as before, until the wound is entirely closed;  

et cout la plaie.  
and sew the wound.  

Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:  
The heads burn off in the intestine and cause no harm to the patient, and the intestine can also be tied with a fine thread made from the intestine of an animal, in this way:  

pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;  
Take the end of this thread from the intestine, which should be very clean, then tie a fine twisted linen thread to its end, then thread it through a needle, sew the intestine, and return it to the rupture.  

et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;  
And this method of sewing with clamps is nothing but a path of confidence and hope;  

et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.  
And if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the small intestines, there is neither art nor health to be found, except through great delicacy.  

de fistule ou qu’ele soit  
Of a fistula, wherever it may be  

Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.  
Know that any wound or abscess, when it grows old, is universally called a “fistula,” especially when it is hardened and emits pus.  

Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;  
And a fistula is, in truth, a hardened and whitish knotty swelling where no pain is felt, and it is as closed as the quill of a bird.  

et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;  
And sometimes clear pus escapes from it, and other times thick;  

aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;  
sometimes little, and other times a great deal;  

et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:  
And I have already spoken of this in the classification of wounds, that any wound that does not heal and has no flesh, is due only to one of nine causes:  

c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;  
namely, the smallness of the blood or the body;  

ou por sa malice;  
or its malignancy;  

ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;  
or because there is hard flesh within it or on its lips, preventing new flesh from forming;  

ou il i a trop de bowe;  
or there is too much pus;  

ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;  
or the area is rotten, and the matter is of poor quality;  

ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;  
or the medicine used in the treatment is not effective;  

ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;  
or because the corruption is of a pestilential nature;  

ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;  
or because the nature of the region causes delayed digestion, slow healing, and natural swelling;  

ou il i a voinnes ou os:  
or there are veins or bones present:  

et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.  
And I have already shown all these causes, their signs, and their treatments in the classification.  

Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.  
Now it is necessary that I explain to you the treatment of a fistula that is done by manual operation.  

Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;  
Know that fistulas occur in all parts of the body;  

car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;  
for there are fistulas that come to the large veins, and to the arteries, and to the nerves, or to the diaphragm, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to certain ribs, or to the spine, or to any joint of the hands or feet;  

et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.  
and there are some that occur in the essence of a principal member, and in similar places.  

Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;  
And all the fistulas of this nature are difficult to heal, and there is nothing but effort and ignorance.  

et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;  
And if there is any fistula that does not reach the places I have mentioned, and you are confident of the cure, and you want to examine it, then take a probe of bronze or iron, and if the fistula is straight, explore it;  

et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;  
and if the fistula is twisted, examine it with a fine probe of lead, for lead bends easily around the twists;  

et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;  
and if the fistula has several openings and you cannot examine it well with probes, then inject it through one of the openings, for the moisture will flow from one opening to another and cleanse it;  

puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;  
then carefully examine it as best as you can, to determine if there is bone or nerve involved, and if it ends deeply, and ask the patient well about the pain he feels when you press with your hand, and where he feels it;  

et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;  
and when you truly know the location where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery, or a vein, or in one of the places I mentioned to you, then cut it according to what I have told you, and remove the foulness and the decayed flesh inside;  

et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;  
and then treat it until it is healed, and if the fistula is very deep and straight, you must cut it deeply, as far as you can, then place probes moistened with a sharp medicine, and insert them to the end of the fistula, so that the medicine corrodes the excess tissue remaining at the bottom;  

et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;  
and then apply ointments that generate healthy flesh, until it is healed;  

et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.  
and if it is not healed by this, cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, cut it.  

Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;  
If neither vein nor nerve nor principal members trouble you, as we have said;  

et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;  
and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, scrape it until all the corruption is removed, then treat it with things that generate flesh until it is healed;  

et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:  
and if it is not healed, and pus continues to flow as before, know that you have not reached the bottom:  

si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;  
then uncover and search until you reach the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore the site;  

et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.  
and if it is healed thus, it is good.  

Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;  
If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach;  

si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;  
there is no other remedy than to leave it to nature;  

et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;  
and if there is a small corrupted bone, and you can extract it with forceps, extract it with a suitable instrument, and if there are several bones, extract them all, leaving not a single one;  

et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.  
and if the moisture troubles you, and there is no error or fear, then cut away the moisture and flesh, and expose the bones.  

Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;  
And if you cannot remove them all at once, apply to the wound something that generates rot, and leave it until the area around the bones is rotted, and then the bones will come out more easily;  

et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;  
and if it is a large bone, such as from the leg or thigh, scrape only the corrupted part until all the blackness is removed, then restore the wound;  

et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;  
and if a large part of it is corrupted and it reaches the marrow of the bone;  

si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;  
then it must be filed and cut down to the corruption, and then treated until it is joined;  

et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.  
and I will tell you about a fistula that occurred in a man’s leg, so that you may take example and aid from it in your work.  

Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;  
There was a young man of about 30 years who had pain in his leg due to an internal cause, so much so that the substances came to his leg, and it became swollen with a large abscess, and there was no external reason to open it.  

mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;  
But the doctors, through their recklessness, worked on it so much that the abscess opened, and a lot of matter flowed out, and it became a fistula, and many openings appeared, all of which discharged pus and moisture from the body.  

et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;  
And many doctors treated it for about two years, but there was no one skilled in the art of surgery until I was called, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which they were treating it, and the substances flowing copiously from the openings.  

et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.  
And the young man's body was becoming red and had a sallow color.  

Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.  
I inserted a probe into one of these openings, and then examined all the openings and found that one connected to the other from all parts of the leg.  

Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;  
I then hastened and cut into one of the openings until I exposed a part of the bone, and I found it corrupted and perforated, and the corruption extended into the bone.  

je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;  
I sawed away the part of the corrupted bone that was visible to me and thought there was no other corruption except what I had removed.  

et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;  
And I began to treat the wound with healing medicines over a long time, but it could not heal.  

et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;  
And then I started again, exposed the bone as before, and found the corruption continuing in the bone; I sawed it, removed it, and worked to heal the site.  

mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;  
But I could not succeed until I cut around a palm’s length of the bone and removed it entirely, then treated it with medicines.  

et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.  
And he was healed and cured quickly, and there was no need to restart the work except due to the patient’s weakness, as he could not endure it, and because of the fear I had for his life.  

Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.  
For due to the evacuation, he often bled, but he was completely healed, and in place of the bone, a hard flesh grew, which was of good quality and caused no harm or hindrance whatsoever, neither in walking nor in movement.  

Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:  
And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it must be sawed in this manner:  

pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;  
Take a cord, and tie it to the end of the bone that is exposed, and instruct someone to pull it upward.  

et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;  
Then take another cord of wool, thicker than the first cord, and tie it over the flesh above the bone, and stretch it, so that you draw the corrupted flesh downward and expose the flesh over the site where you want to saw, ensuring that the saw does not harm the flesh.  

et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;  
And place a stick or a board beneath the bone to stabilize it while cutting the corrupted flesh.  

et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.  
And it is necessary to saw as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and saw again if needed.  

Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;  
And if the bone is corrupted but not exposed, and the corruption is in the middle or in a section, then uncover all the flesh.  

puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;  
Then place a stick beneath, and then saw from one end of the corruption to the other, with the sawing following the length of the corruption as we have said.  

et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;  
And if the corruption is in the joint, then cut the corrupted joint and saw the bone where it connects on the other side.  

et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;  
And if the corruption is at the connection of two joints, then there is no remedy other than cutting.  

et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;  
And if the corruption is in the wrist of the hand or the ankle of the foot, it is very difficult, but you must still investigate this corrosion and determine how it manifests.  

et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;  
And clean it in every way you can, provided the veins or nerves do not cause you trouble.  

et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;  
And know that the knives and saws for cutting these bones are of many types, according to the position of the bones, their appearance, their thickness, their delicacy, their size, their smallness, and their hardness.  

et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;  
And thus it is necessary to prepare the instrument suited to each kind of operation.  

et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;  
And know that the work will show you the instrument you will need, according to the knowledge of this art and the observation of the forms of the diseases.  

si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.  
Thus, consider carefully the instrument you need according to what is required.  

dou feu  
Of fire.  

Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;  
The flesh rots either from an internal cause or from an external cause.  

et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;  
And when you have treated this corrosion with medicinal cures and they do not work, it is necessary to cut that limb up to where the corrosion extends, so that the patient escapes death or, worse, the harm caused by the loss of the limb.  

et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;  
And the signs are that the limb becomes black, so that it seems as though it has been burned by fire, and it rots after the blackening; then the corrosion spreads from limb to limb and takes over the entire body.  

si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.  
So hasten to cut it, and if it is caused by the sting of some venomous creatures, like a sea scorpion or a viper or similar, if the corrosion is at the tip of the finger, then cut it off and do not let it reach the hand.  

Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;  
And if it reaches the hand, cut it off at the joint so that the corrosion does not reach the arm.  

et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;  
And if it reaches the arm, cut it off at the elbow.  

et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;  
And if it passes the elbow, it is death, and no remedy will help except the amount of his strength.  

et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:  
And do the same when the corrosion reaches the foot.  

s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;  
If it reaches the first joint, cut it after the next joint.  

et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;  
And if it reaches the foot, cut off the entire foot.  

et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;  
And if it rises to the leg, cut it off at the knee joint.  

et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;  
And if it goes above the knee, there is no other solution than to leave the patient to die.  

et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;  
And the method for cutting or sawing the limb is that you tie it above and below, and one assistant pulls one tie downward and another assistant pulls the other tie upward, and you sever the flesh between the two ties to a width of one span, so that the bone is exposed.  

puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.  
Then cut or saw it, and place on each side a piece of linen cloth so that the saw does not touch the healthy area and cause the patient another wound or a hot abscess.  

Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;  
And if blood flow comes during the operation, cauterize the site quickly or apply some astringent powders.  

puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;  
Then return to your medicine until the procedure is complete, then bind the injured limb with an appropriate bandage and treat it until it is healed.  

et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:  
And I will tell you what happened to a man concerning his foot.  

il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;  
He developed a blackening that seemed like a burn from fire, and this corrosion first appeared in his toe, until it affected the whole foot.  

et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;  
And when the man saw the corrosion, he hurried to cut off his foot, and he was healed.  

et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;  
And a long time later, the corrosion returned in a finger of his hand, and he came to me, and I applied counteracting treatments after purifying the body, but the corrosion could not stop.  

et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;  
And he wanted me to cut off his hand, but I did not wish to, as I had hope of counteracting the condition.  

et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;  
And I also feared that if I amputated his hand, he might die, as the man's strength was weak.  

et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;  
And he despaired completely, returned to his land, hurried to cut off his hand, and was healed.  

et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.  
And I have recounted this only so that one may do likewise, if needed.  

Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;  
Sometimes an abscess appears in a fleshy area and remains so long that it causes a large accumulation of pus.  

et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;  
Then it bursts and opens, and the pus flows out, leaving the area hollow, like a vessel.  

et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;  
And the skin above it is as thin as a delicate cloth and does not reach the bone or the nerve, and such a condition is called a “sain” and not a “fistula.”  

mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;  
But if it is so deep that it reaches the bone, it is called a “fistula.”  

et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;  
And the treatment is that you cut away all the skin around it, especially when it is thin, like a cloth.  

et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.  
And this is necessary because of its corruption.  

Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:  
And if you believe that the skin is inflamed, and the corruption is not deep, and the skin is thick with flesh, treat it with a clyster in this way:  

regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:  
observe if the swelling is large, and the discharge that flows from it has a foul odor, then treat it with an Egyptian medicine prepared in this way:  

prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;  
take garlic, oil, and litharge in equal parts, and cook them in a vessel over the fire until the medicine becomes red and as thick as honey;  

et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;  
then take from it as needed, dissolve it in water and honey, and use it to cleanse the swelling, squeezing out the opening;  

et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;  
and leave the medicine in for two hours, then extract it by pressing;  

fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;  
do this many times until the swelling is cleansed and the stench is removed;  

et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;  
and sometimes it is cleansed with ash water when this medicine is unavailable, which is made by taking vinewood ashes, pouring water over them, then straining it, and using it to cleanse until you are sure the swelling is well purified;  

et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;  
and if the patient cannot tolerate it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the ash water, then cleanse it with water and honey mixed with a little ground litharge;  

ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;  
or cleanse it with a mixture of honey and wine, as honey has the property of cleaning and washing, and wine causes the swelling to dry out;  

et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;  
and when you have done this and believe the swelling is well cleaned, treat it with something that promotes the growth of flesh in it, such as diafin plaster mixed with rose oil and wine;  

ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;  
or cleanse it with certain medicines and ointments whose properties I have described in the treatise on ointments;  

et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;  
and if the opening of the swelling is small and the nozzle of the cleanser cannot enter, enlarge it slightly with a tool, and insert a plug of Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment, so that it becomes widened;  

et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.  
and if the wound is too large, sew it up, leaving only an opening through which the cleanser can enter, and if the opening from which the discharge flows is above, cut it lower;  

Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;  
For when the pus is deep, do not allow flesh to grow there;  

et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:  
and if you cannot cut the breast below as you wish, arrange it so that the pus flows to the lowest place where it is, for when the pus is deep, do not allow flesh to grow there, and if you cannot cut the breast below as you wish, arrange it in such a manner:  

que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;  
that the pus flows easily downward, and leave none of the pus there;  

et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;  
and take consolidative medicines to apply to the breast, and spread them on a linen cloth that covers the entire breast;  

puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;  
then cut with scissors at the opening of the breast a little larger than the first, then spread a soft ointment on another cloth according to the size of the opening, and place it on the opening of the breast to ease the pus, and do not remove the large cloth except after many days, once;  

et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;  
and the one on the opening of the breast, remove it often to take out the pus, and note what flows from the pus, whether it is venomous or little or much, digested or undigested;  

et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;  
and observe whether the patient feels pain or not, and whether there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine is applied in this manner and you see the tissue springing up over the opening of the breast, then know that the breast is already healing, and health is approaching;  

et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.  
and then untie it in the morning or on the third day, and when you untie the wound, replace the cloth and renew the ointment.  

Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.  
And if the breast expels undigested pus after many days, know that the breast is not healing.  

Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.  
And if subtle venom flows after a long time, do not despair of healing, for health is approaching.  

Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;  
For there are men whose flesh is slow to grow in their wounds, and others in whom the opposite occurs;  

et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;  
and if undigested pus springs from the breast after many days, know that the breast is not healing;  

et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;  
and if the breast is slow to heal and delayed, add medicines that are moist in substance and dry in virtue, such as the ointment called diafinit, for it contains a large part of vitriol, and it is the ultimate medicine;  

pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;  
take the ointment diafinit, and prepare it with rose oil, and sprinkle it with aged wine equal in substance;  

puis le confit et en use;  
then preserve it and use it;  

et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;  
and this same effect is achieved by well-cooked thickened honey, when the ointment diafinit is not available, or you take myrrh, aloe, and incense, grind them, and powder them over the honey while it is on the fire;  

et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;  
and then soak a cloth in it, and spread it over the breast, and sometimes administer long aristolochia and roots of heavenly lily, which is like the flour of vetch and centaury;  

et en use de simples ou de compostes:  
and use these in simple or composite form:  

broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;  
grind them, make a powder, and put it on the honey I mentioned, and use it;  

et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;  
and if the cure is prolonged, and is not achieved through this treatment, then know that the corruption is deep, and has affected the bone, the hard tissues, or the ligaments;  

si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.  
then treat it as a case of fistula, as we have said previously.  

de l’aposteme de l’ungle  
Of the abscess of the nail  

Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;  
A whitlow is an abscess that forms beneath the nail of the finger of the hand, or the foot, or sometimes forms on other fingers;  

et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;  
and when it becomes chronic, and no attention is paid to it, a hot abscess forms there, spreads, and expels pus to such an extent that it reaches the root of the nail, and sometimes consumes it entirely;  

et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.  
and the corrosion reaches the bone, causing a foul-smelling pain, and the tip of the finger becomes swollen, and its color darkens.  

Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.  
When you treat it as we have explained in the division, and the treatment does not succeed, you must cut away all the remnants of the nail with a blade, then cauterize the wound afterward.  

Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;  
The cautery is a great help if the bone is healthy, and the nail is sound.  

et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;  
and if the nail presses into the flesh and begins to puncture and injure it, you must insert a wedge under the nail where it pierces the flesh, lift it upward, and carefully cut away that flesh gently, then apply burning and corrosive medicines to remove all of it;  

puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.  
then treat it with ointments until it is healed.  

Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;  
And if the corrosion has reached the bone, cut it and remove it, for as long as the corrupted bone remains, it cannot heal;  

et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;  
and if you see the finger decaying, cut it off at one of the joints as previously described, then treat it until it is healed;  

et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;  
and if it is struck and inflamed, and there is great pain, you must first bleed it;  

puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;  
then cut the nail with a sharp spatumile, cutting across above it, and ensure that the cut does not reach the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too great pain;  

et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.  
and if this happens, apply something to ease the pain.  

la dolor dou sourdoit de la main  
The pain of the supernumerary finger of the hand  

Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.  
The extra fingers that appear on the hands of some men are sometimes entirely fleshy, sometimes they contain bones, and sometimes they have nails, and some of them grow at the root of the joint, or the growth occurs in certain joints of the fingers.  

Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;  
Those that grow on some joints of the finger do not move, but those that grow at the joint of the finger sometimes do move;  

la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:  
The removal of the fleshy one is simple, as follows:  

taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.  
Cut it at its root with a broad spatumile.  

Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:  
Those that grow at the root of the joint are difficult to treat:  

si te tien dou coper.  
so refrain from cutting.  

En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.  
For one that grows on the back joint of the finger, you must first cut the flesh circularly down to the bone, then cut the bone with an appropriate saw, and then treat it until it is healed.  

Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.  
The joining that occurs between fingers happens from birth, or by adhesion of a wound, or by burning with fire, or by similar causes.  

Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;  
You must cut this adhesion so that the fingers regain their natural forms;  

puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;  
then place between them tents or cloths soaked in rose oil, so that they do not adhere again;  

ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.  
or place between them thin pieces of lead until the area heals as it should.  

Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.  
If adhesion occurs between one of these fingers and the palm, cut this adhesion as necessary.  

des vils  
Of boils  

Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;  
Boils are swollen veins filled with melancholic superfluities, which occur in various parts of the body;  

et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.  
and they occur more frequently on the legs of those who walk, work, and carry loads than on others.  

Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.  
It is necessary, therefore, to administer purging of the bile at times, and then treat them with basilicum ointment.  

Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:  
The treatment with iron is of two types:  

l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;  
one is to cut them and draw out the black blood;  

et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.  
and the other method is to lift the vein and extract it entirely.  

Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:  
The cutting is done in this manner:  

arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;  
First, bathe the leg in very hot water so that the thick blood becomes thinned, then bind the patient's leg from above the thigh down to the part below the knee.  

puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;  
Then cut the vein in one place, or in two or three, with a wide incision, and draw out the black blood with your hand from one end to the other, until as much blood as the patient's strength can bear has been let out.  

et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;  
Then bind it, and instruct him to abstain from foods that generate black bile.  

et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.  
And resume the evacuation and the bleeding when the veins are full, and it harms the patient.  

Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:  
The removal of it is done in this manner:  

reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;  
Raise the patient’s leg, if it has much hair, then place it in a bath and bathe the leg in hot water until it becomes red and the veins swell.  

et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;  
And if you do not have a bath, warm it by the fire, and then cut along the vein either at the top of the knee or in the part below near the ankle.  

puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;  
Then open the skin with a hook and strip the vein on each side until it is visible to the touch.  

et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;
