And it appears red and black, and when it enters the skin, it looks like a white cord.  

puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;  
Then insert the hook beneath it until it is raised from the skin, and then hang it gently on a hook, then cut it in another place three fingers higher.  

puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;  
Then strip the skin over the vein until it is visible, then raise it with the hook as you did before, and hang it on another hook as you did the first.  

puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;  
Then make another cut, or several if needed, then raise it and cut it at the toe of the foot, then draw and raise it up to the second cut.  

puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;  
Then pull it out cut by cut until it is entirely out, then sever it.  

et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;  
And if you cannot pull and raise it, insert a needle with a strong double thread, tie it, pull it, insert a hook beneath it, and twist your hand from one side to the other until it comes out.  

et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;  
And take care not to let it break, for if it breaks, it cannot be pulled or raised, and harm will come to the patient.  

et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;  
And when you have entirely removed it, place over the wound site wool soaked in wine and rose oil.  

et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.  
And treat it until it is healed.  

Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;  
And if the vein is constricted, twisted, and coiled together, and it is not straight as we have said, you must slit it crookedly but not cut it.  

et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.  
And pull it as we have described before.  

Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;  
The shape of the tool used to cut the vein is curved and does not slice so as not to cut the vein.  

et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:  
And it is of a thick curve, for if it were thin, it would cut the vein, but it must be thick as we have said, and here is its shape:  

de la voinne civile  
Of the civil vein  

Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;  
This vein forms in the legs, in warm regions where no grass or trees grow, and in lands without moisture.  

et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.  
And it may sometimes form elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens from putrefaction that arises beneath the skin, as serpents and worms form within the body, nestled between skin and flesh.  

Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.  
And the signs of the onset of this vein are that a very great inflammation appears in the leg, then the place changes, and the vein begins to protrude, like the root of a plant.  

Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;  
When the head appears, you must wrap it around with a piece of lead weighing one and a half to two ounces, and tie it, leaving the lead hanging from the leg, and each time a part emerges outside, wrap it around the lead and tie it.  

et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;  
And if it is too long, cut off a portion and wrap the remainder, but do not cut it at the root until it is completely removed.  

car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;  
For if you cut it, it will retreat into the flesh and cause an abscess and decay at the site, and severe illness.  

por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;  
For this reason, it must be drawn out little by little to the end, leaving nothing behind in the body.  

et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;  
And sometimes this vein, when removed, is five handspans long or even ten. A man once came to me whose vein was ten handspans long, and when you cut it, insert a hook or probe and pierce it deeply so that it is entirely removed.  

et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.  
And the material inside must be emptied, and apply medicines to the site to counteract putrefaction for some days, then treat it as with abscesses.  

Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;  
And sometimes this vein has fewer roots, especially when it appears at the joint of the foot or in the foot, where many openings appear and roots sprout.  

cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.  
Treat it then as we have described above.  

des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char  
Of worms that are born between skin and flesh  

Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;  
This disease is called in our land "ox disease" because it often occurs in oxen, and it is a small worm born between skin and flesh, which travels throughout the body, ascending and descending, and can be felt as it moves from limb to limb until it pierces the skin where it travels and emerges.  

et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;  
And it is generated by the decay of certain humors, just as worms, serpents, earthworms, and ascarids arise in the belly.  

et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;  
And its malice is feared, for when it travels through the body, and ascends to the head, and reaches the eye, it sometimes enters and destroys the eye.  

et ceu avient maintes fois.  
And this happens often.  

Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:  
When you wish to treat and remove it, it can only be drawn out when it is moving.  

si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;  
Thus, you must bind the area above and below it with a strong and tight band, then cut above and draw it out. If the worm is deep in the flesh and you cannot find it, cauterize the area with fire until it dies.  

et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;  
And the greatest harm it causes is that it destroys the eye, as we have said.  

et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;  
And if you see it moving toward the head near the eye, press tightly beneath the eyebrow, then cut above and draw it out.  

et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.  
And the patient must undergo purification of the body with dissolving medicines for the corrupted humors, and abstain from foods that generate putrefaction.  

de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit  
Of pain caused by windiness  

Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;  
This disease is called in our land "vakirir," and it is a pain that occurs in certain limbs and can then move from limb to limb.  

et je vis ceu que je vos di.  
And I have seen what I tell you.  

Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;  
I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm.  

et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;  
And shortly after, I saw it rise like a worm to the shoulder, faster than anything, like quicksilver as it moves from one place to another.  

li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;  
The pain left that place and lodged in the shoulder, and then shortly after ran throughout the body until it reached the other arm.  

puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.  
Then she told me that it kept moving around her body, as I had seen.  

Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.  
I marveled greatly at how it moved thus from limb to limb, for I had never seen this disease behave in this manner.  

Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;  
Nevertheless, I had seen many cases where pain moved from one place to another, but I had never seen it as I did in this woman.  

et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;  
And I thought it was because the woman had a dry body and exposed veins, and thus this constrained windiness appeared.  

et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.  
And this does not appear in those who are delicate, with moist bodies and covered veins.  

Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;  
And when you wish to treat this illness, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears to you as we have said, then quickly bind it above and below, and then cut over it until that swelling, forced into place, escapes outward;  

et cauterize le leu;  
and cauterize the spot;  

et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.  
and if you do not see it with your eyes, treat it with something that expels swelling, such as fetid pills, serapin pills, and similar remedies.  

des saiettes  
Of arrows  

Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.  
Arrows are diverse, according to their forms and the parts of the body where they strike.  

Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;  
The diversity among them is that there are those with large points, and small ones, and those that are barbed and welded;  

et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;  
and those with two edges, and those with tongues, and those made of segments;  

et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:  
and those that strike a limb do so in two ways:  

ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.  
either in a principal organ, such as the brain, heart, liver, lung, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar organs.  

Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:  
When it strikes any of these places, and the signs of death, which I will tell you shortly, appear to you:  

si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;  
then you must refrain from extracting this arrow, for death will follow in many circumstances;  

et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.  
and when these bad signs do not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then extract it, and treat the wound.  

Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;  
The signs for the brain when an arrow strikes it and pierces the bone, and the cerebral fluid that is above the brain escapes, include dizziness, sudden fainting, vertigo, redness in the eyes, inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasms and confusion of thought, and vomiting of bile;  

et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;  
and sometimes it escapes in fluid from the nostrils or ears;  

et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;  
and sometimes speech and voice are lost;  

et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;  
and from the wound escapes a white moisture resembling pus, and sometimes also fragments of flesh;  

et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.  
and if these signs appear to you, refrain from treatment, and do not extract the arrow if it is embedded.  

Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;  
The signs for the arrow when it strikes the heart are that it is near the left breast, and it feels as though it is fixed in something hard, not hollow;  

et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:  
and sometimes the arrow moves as the pulse does, and black blood flows, and coldness and cold sweat occur, and fainting:  

saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.  
then know without doubt that death is near.  

Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.  
The signs of an arrow that injures the lung are that blood full of foam escapes from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, breathes heavily, and seeks cool air.  

Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;  
And if the arrow strikes the covering of the chest, it is near the lower ribs;  

et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;  
and there is heavy breathing and great pain and sighing;  

et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.  
and all the parts of the shoulders move.  

Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.  
And if the arrow strikes the stomach, sometimes undigested food escapes from the wound.  

Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.  
And if the arrow strikes the abdomen, and fecal matter escapes through the wound in the intestines, then there is no hope for a cure or for extracting the arrow.  

Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:  
And if the arrow strikes the bladder, and urine escapes and flows outward, and the patient feels severe pain:  

saiches que li plaie est mortelz.  
know that the wound is fatal.  

Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.  
The other parts, such as the face, the neck, the throat, the shoulders, the arms, the spine, the buttocks, the thighs, and the legs, and similar members, are safe in many cases.  

Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.  
When the arrow is in a nerve or an artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you happened to me, so that you may act in the same way.  

Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:  
It happened to a man that an arrow fell into his tear duct at the root of his nose:  

je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.  
I examined it and extracted it from the other side beneath the fat of the ear, and he was healed without complications.  

Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;  
And I extracted an arrow from an eye, which had fallen into the fat of the eye beneath the eyelid, and the arrow was lodged, and I could only reach its point near the shaft, and the arrow was large, from a Turkish bow, with a light head without barbs;  

li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.  
the eye was healed, and no bad complications occurred.  

Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:  
And I extracted an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arabian arrow with barbs:  

je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.  
I smoothed the barbs and worked delicately until I extracted it, and the Christian was healed.  

Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;  
And I extracted an arrow from a man, which had fallen into his belly, and I thought he would die;  

et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;  
and after thirty days had passed, his condition had not changed;  

je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.  
I cut above the arrow, manipulated it, and extracted it, and there were no bad complications.  

Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;  
And I saw a man into whose back an arrow had fallen, and the wound was sealed over;  

et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.  
and the arrow remained inside him, and his natural functions did not change, nor did he experience any harm in any of his natural actions.  

Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;  
And I saw another man into whose face an arrow had fallen, and the wound was sealed;  

et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;  
and he remained thus without suffering great pain;  

et mout d’autres semblans.  
and many other similar cases.  

Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;  
And I extracted an arrow from a man among the king's princes, which had fallen into the middle of his nose, and was slightly inclined to the right side;  

et estoit li saiette toute reponue.  
and the arrow was entirely lodged.  

Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.  
I was called to treat it three days after it had fallen.  

Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.  
I found the wound very narrow.  

Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;  
I probed it with a fine probe and could not feel it;  

et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.  
and he felt pricking and pain beneath his right ear.  

Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette. Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; 
I thought it was from the arrow's point. I applied an adhesive and digestive plaster to the spot so that the area would not swell;  

et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.  
and the location of the arrow became apparent to me.  

Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;  
I applied the plaster for several days, and the wound healed again, and the patient remained like this for a long time, until one day he felt the arrow inside his nose;  

et il le me dist.  
and he told me about it.  

Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;  
I applied a corrosive, sharp medicine to the wound for several days, until it opened, and I probed it and felt the head of the arrow embedded in the spot;  

puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;  
then I added more of that sharp medicine to the opening of the wound, until the head of the arrow became visible to me;  

et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;  
and about four months passed, and then the wound widened enough that I inserted the pincers, moved it from one side to the other, and it could not come out;  

adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.  
then I did not stop delicately working and manipulating with different instruments until one day I grasped it with well-made pincers, as their design will be described at the end of this chapter, and I extracted it and restored the wound.  

Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:  
And the physicians judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored:  

je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.  
I restored it, then, and the wound healed, and the patient was completely cured.  

Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;  
Now I have told you the details of extracting certain arrows, so that you may apply your skill to what I do not say, for the book cannot encompass everything;  

mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.  
but the wise master draws great knowledge from little, and based on what is present and what is missing, discovers new procedures and new instruments for addressing the strange occurrences that arise in this art.  

Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:  
I say that arrows can only be removed from the parts where they are lodged in two ways:  

ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;  
either through the place where they entered, or through another spot;  

et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.  
and those that exit through where they entered are arrows lodged in fleshy areas, and they sometimes come out immediately.  

Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;  
And if it does not come out immediately, then leave it until the flesh rots around it, and the way out is eased;  

et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;  
and likewise, if it is lodged in the bone and cannot come out, then leave it like this for several days, and move it daily;  

et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.  
and then it will come out, and if it does not, then pierce around it with a fine drill until the area around it is widened, and then extract it.  

Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:  
And if the arrow is lodged in the bone of the skull and reaches one of the ventricles of the brain, and any of the symptoms I have described appear in the patient:  

si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.  
then do not extract it, but leave it until it becomes stable after some days, because if the arrow reaches the meninges, it is death.  

Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.  
And if the arrow is only lodged in the bone and does not reach the meninges, and the patient remains for some days without bad complications, then proceed with extraction.  

Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;  
And if it is deeply lodged and cannot come out, then use drills around it, as I have described;  

puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.  
then treat the area until it is healed.  

Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;  
And if the arrow is lodged in a part of the body so that it cannot be seen, then search for it with a probe;  

et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;  
and if you feel it, then extract it with a suitable instrument;  

et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;  
and if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone, nerve, or vein in the way, then widen the wound until it is large enough;  

et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;  
and extract the arrow if you can, and if the arrow has barbs by which it holds, then remove the flesh embedded in them on both sides as much as you can, and then break or bend the barbs of the arrow until you can extract it;  

et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.  
and work carefully so as not to break the arrow, for extracting it would then become more difficult.  

Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.  
And if you cannot extract it at once, then leave it until the surrounding area becomes rotten, and then extract it, for the extraction will be easier.  

Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;  
And if the flow of blood opposes you, then administer what we have discussed regarding treatment in its chapter;  

et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;  
and beware of cutting into a nerve or vein, and plan how you can remove the arrow without danger, whether quickly or slowly, forcefully or gently;  

et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.  
and position the patient in the way he was when the arrow fell into him, for that is the greatest aid there is, and if you cannot, then position him as the signs indicate to you.  

Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:  
An arrow that comes out the other side, where something of it is visible, or where the skin is swollen so that it can be seen or felt clearly:  

taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:  
then cut above it, so that the pincers can grip it, and then extract it:  

si saut fuer maintenant.  
and it will come out immediately.  

Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.  
And if it is stuck in the bone, then rotate your hand gently, so that it enters the bone and widens it, then extract it.  

Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;  
And if it cannot come out, then leave it again, and then restart the extraction until it comes out;  

et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;  
and if the shaft of the arrow is there, then push it out with the shaft;  

et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;  
and if the shaft has fallen off, and you want to apply pressure, then use a capped instrument so that the point of the arrow enters the cap of the instrument;  

et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.  
and then push it out, and if the arrow is broken, then use an instrument with an inward-pointing tip to ease the extraction.  

Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.  
And if the arrow is poisoned, then it is necessary to cut away all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as needed.  

Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;  
And if the arrow falls into the foot, the belly, the bladder, or the side, and it is near the surface, and you can cut above it, then cut;  

et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;  
and take care not to cut the vein or the nerve, and then extract it, and then sew the wound, if necessary;  

et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.  
and treat it until it is healed.  

Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:  
The shape of the pincers used to extract arrows resembles the beak of a bird, and here is the design:  

Et en sont mout de manieres:  
And there are many types:  

grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.  
large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the arrow.  

Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:  
The shape of the capped pusher is also like the quill of a bird, to press against the point of the arrow, as this design shows:  

li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:  
the design of the pincers for pressing and pulling is as follows:  

des voinnes dou cors communes  
Of the veins of the common body  

Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:  
There are thirty-one veins for bleeding, of which sixteen are in the head, namely:  

II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;  
Two pulsating veins behind the ears, which are called the two "herbech";  

et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;  
And the two arteries visible in the temples;  

et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;  
And two veins in the tear ducts of the eyes, which are called "aspires";  

et li voine que est emmi le front;  
And the vein in the middle of the forehead;  

et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;  
And the vein at the tip of the nose;  

et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;  
And the two guindeges in the neck;  

et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;  
And the two veins in the lips above the mouth, which are called "augeherich";  

et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.  
And two veins beneath the tongue.  

Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:  
The veins commonly used for bleeding are five in each arm:  

l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;  
One is the cephalic vein, on the left side, called by common folk the "head vein";  

et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;  
The middle one is called "faste," composed of the cephalic and basilic veins, and commonly called the "heart vein";  

et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.  
The basilic vein is on the right side, called by common folk the "belly vein," located on the fold, and it is the one most clearly visible on the wrist.  

Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;  
The salvatelle is the vein between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches;  

et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:  
And in the leg and foot, there are three veins:  

l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;  
One is below the curve of the hollow on the left side, the second is the saphenous vein at the ankle on the right side;  

et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;  
And the vein called "nesse," which is at the ankle on the other side;  

et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.  
And in the other leg, there are three veins below these.  

Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;  
Bleeding from the veins behind the ears helps with chronic catarrh and migraines;  

et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;  
And the procedure for bleeding, as I tell you, is to raise the patient's head and rub the area of the veins with a coarse cloth;  

puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:  
Then the patient's neck is tightened with a band, so the two veins appear behind the ears in two places connected to the head:  

quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;  
Find them with your finger, and where you feel the pulse beneath your finger, there bleed on one side;  

puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;  
Then take the lancet and insert it beneath the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand along the vein, cutting both the skin and the vein by about two finger-widths, letting the blood flow as much as you wish;  

puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;  
Then bind it tightly until it heals;  

et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.  
And I have already explained the incision and cauterization in the first book.  

Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;  
Bleeding from the two arteries in the temples is effective for chronic migraines, sudden migraines, persistent ophthalmia, and sharp tear pains in the eyes;  

et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:  
And the procedure for bleeding is as I describe:  

et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;  
The patient tightens their neck so that the two veins become clearly visible;  

et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;  
Feel the pulse under your finger, and then bleed on one side;  

puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;  
Then lift the vein upward with your index finger, insert the lancet beneath it, elevate the vein, and cut it as you have done with the other two veins, letting the blood flow according to your need;  

puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;  
Then untie the patient, press your finger on the vein for an hour, and afterward apply cotton to it;  

et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;  
Then bind it tightly and leave it until it is healed;  

et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.  
And we have already spoken about their cutting and extraction in the beginning of the book.  

Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;  
Bleeding from the vein in the forehead is as effective as bleeding from the cephalic vein for chronic facial diseases, migraines, and redness;  

et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;  
And the procedure is that the patient tightens their neck while twisting it so that the vein becomes visible;  

puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:  
Then take the instrument called "fosseur," whose form is as follows:  

Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;  
Place its point on the vein, strike it with your hand or another object, and let the blood flow according to the quantity you desire;  

puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit sanee, et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.  
Then release the patient's neck and bind the vein until it heals, sometimes using a wide flame for the procedure.  

Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;  
Nevertheless, the lancet must not be too sharp;  

et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.  
Bleed it crosswise, for the bone is near, and the lancet may break if it is too delicate.  

Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;  
Bleeding from the two veins in the tear ducts helps the eyes, scaly eruptions, redness, swelling in the eye, and facial diseases;  

et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;  
And the procedure for their bleeding is for the patient to tighten their neck by twisting it with some band, as described before;  

puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.  
Then bleed it, making the incision crosswise and slightly along the length with a somewhat wide lancet, as there is little flesh there.  

Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;  
If the lancet is too delicate, it might break.  

puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.  
Let the blood flow as much as needed, then apply cotton and bind it tightly.  

Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;  
Bleeding from the vein in the nose is effective for acute fevers, sudden fits of madness, facial diseases such as migraines and redness of the face, especially when chronic;  

et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;  
The procedure for the bleeding is for the patient to tighten their neck, then for you to pinch their nose with your left hand and take a long, delicate lancet. Insert it into the space in the middle of the lip, between the two nostrils, since the vein is not easily visible there, and the blood will immediately begin to flow.  

et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;  
Do not go too deep, let the blood flow as needed, then bind it for the night, as it heals very quickly.  

et c’est li forme dou flaime:  
And this is the form of the lancet:  

Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;  
Bleeding from the two guindeges helps with constriction of the groin, the onset of leprosy, many illnesses, scabs, corrosive ulcers, herpes, and tumors.  

et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;  
The procedure for this bleeding is for the patient to tighten their neck beneath one or the other vein, as we have mentioned.  

et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;  
The practitioner should stand above the patient's head, while the patient sits on a seat. Bleed the vein along its length with a somewhat wide incision, letting the blood flow moderately or as much as needed.  

puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;  
Then repeat the procedure on the other vein, untie the band, and compress both veins moderately so the patient does not choke.  

et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.  
Leave it until morning, so the wound can heal.  

de la sainie des leivres  
On bleeding from the lips  

Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.  
Bleeding from the veins of the upper lips helps with excess moisture in the mouth, gum infections, chapped lips, and nasal issues and their surroundings.  

Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;  
The procedure for this bleeding is to have the patient sit in front of you and tighten their neck as I described.  

puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:  
Then turn the lip and observe the two veins, one on the right side of the lip and the other on the left, recognizable by their dark color and the small black veins surrounding them.  

cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.  
Cut both veins, and if you cannot identify them or are unsure, cut the largest on each side. Do the same with the two veins above and below, as the method is the same.  

de la sainie desoz la lengue  
On bleeding beneath the tongue  

Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;  
Bleeding from the veins beneath the tongue helps after bleeding from the cephalic vein and is useful for throat constriction, uvula diseases, and mouth diseases.  

et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:  
The procedure for this bleeding is to have the patient sit between your hands in the sunlight, lift their tongue, and observe a black vein on each side beneath it.  

saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.  
Bleed both veins, but do not go too deep, as the arteries are beneath them.  

Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:  
The veins in the wrist commonly bled are bled in two ways:  

ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;  
Either by using a wide lancet shaped like a myrtle leaf, or a delicate olive-shaped one resembling a sharp knife, called "anesil";  

et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.  
They are wide or delicate, depending on the width or narrowness of the veins.  

Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:  
The form of the myrtle-leaf lancet is very renowned, and it is as wide as you see:  

Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;  
It is necessary to open the prominent veins filled with thick, visible blood, which contain thick and troubled blood;  

et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:  
and this is the shape of the olive-shaped lancet:  

et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.  
and it is more finely pointed and is for bleeding the fine veins where there is fine citrine-colored blood.  

Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;  
The bleeding of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases beneath the throat, in the neck, chest, and abdomen;  

et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.  
and it is necessary for the surgeon to bleed carefully and to beware of the artery that is below.  

Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;  
And if he cuts the artery and a flow of blood occurs, it must be stanched, as I have said;  

et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.  
and the lancet should not be piercing, but cutting, like a little blade.  

Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;  
And if the basilica does not appear clearly, you must compress it and choose another;  

ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:  
or you seek one of its branches, or you bleed instead the vein in the middle of the arm:  

elle apert manifestement;  
it appears clearly;  

et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.  
and you cut it with the small blade, as we have said.  

Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;  
And if you want to know the location for bleeding, you must first compress the arm and touch the spot until you feel the pulse;  

puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;  
then mark the spot with ink, tie the arm, and cut the vein with the small blade;  

et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:  
and take care not to strike the artery when you see the spot swelling, for it is the artery:  

eschui la donques.  
avoid it then.  

Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:  
And if you see it spurting upward like a child’s urine, and the blood is red and fine, know that it is arterial blood:  

haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;  
then hurry, press your finger on it for a long time, and remove it only if the blood stops, which often happens;  

se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;  
tie the arm and leave it so, and let the patient remain still;  

et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.  
and be cautious, and do not let him move until he is healed.  

Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;  
And if the blood does not stop, overwhelms you, and medicine is not at hand, then cut the artery if it appears, for its ends retract;  

et estainche li sans.  
and staunch the blood.  

Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;  
Take a pistachio bark, split it, take one of the halves and bind it tightly until the next day;  

se li sans estainche, c’est bien;  
if the blood stops, it is good;  

se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;  
if not, treat it as we have said, with powders that staunch blood;  

et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.  
and the stanching is not difficult in many cases because of the smallness of the wound and the tightness of the band on the arm.  

Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;  
Bleeding from the middle vein helps as it draws blood from the upper head and lower body, since it is formed by the basilica and cephalic veins, as we have said;  

et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;  
and the surgeon must beware of the nerve that is below, for if he pricks too deeply and strikes the nerve, it will swell, the healing will be difficult, and perhaps it will not heal;  

et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;  
and this nerve often appears, but if it does not appear in some people due to its subtlety, you must bleed it with the small instrument;  

et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.  
and avoid the nerve to the best of your ability.  

Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.  
And if there is a vein between the two nerves, cut it lengthwise.  

Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;  
The bleeding of the cephalic vein helps as it draws blood from the head and aids the eyes;  

et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.  
and it is necessary to bleed with the olive-shaped or myrtle-shaped lancet, for it is the safest of all veins, as it has neither nerve nor artery below.  

Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;  
However, you must seek the easiest spot, and it does not matter if you fail the first time; you can try again;  

et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.  
and perhaps the spot may swell in some people when the first attempt fails, but it is not a problem.  

La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.  
The quality of the bloodletting is according to your intention.  

Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;  
The first thing you must know about bloodletting is that it is administered only to preserve health and to prevent future illnesses;  

et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:  
and the bloodletting should be done in one of the three veins located on the arm:  

c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;  
namely, the cephalic, the median, and the basilica;  

et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;  
and one must perform bloodletting at the beginning of spring while fasting, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of repletion appear;  

et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.  
and it should be done on the first or third day, two or three hours after dawn.  

Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;  
Bloodletting for illnesses has no fixed time but is done whenever necessary, by day or night, at any hour and at all times;  

et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.  
and children should not be bled until the age of fourteen, nor pregnant women except from the fourth to the seventh month.  

Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.  
Nor should the elderly over sixty years old be bled.  

Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;  
And when someone wishes to be bled, in whatever manner it may be, it is necessary to cleanse the intestines with a mild enema if there is much retained waste, so that the veins do not draw harmful impurities from the intestines to the principal organs;  

ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;  
nor should someone be bled who is excessively full from food, nor one who is drunk, until they are sober, nor those with dropsy;  

et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;  
and one should avoid bleeding after colic, vomiting, diarrhea, excessive sexual activity, labor, wakefulness, fasting, and anything that exhausts the vitality, either of the soul or the body;  

puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;  
then refine the humors, if the blood is thick, by foods, drinks, and medicines, if you have the ability;  

puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;  
then enter a bath, if nothing prohibits it, to refine the blood, and bleed yourself from the vein of the chest around the third hour, as we have said;  

et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;  
and on that day avoid work, strain, lust, and similar activities;  

et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;  
and be cheerful and joyful, and let the bleeder be higher than the person being bled, rub the arm two or three times, then tie the band moderately tight, for if it is too tight or too loose, the blood cannot flow;  

et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;  
then rub the spot with the hands until the veins swell and can be felt;  

puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.  
then moisten the lancet with a little old oil, and place the finger of the left hand on the vein below the spot where he wants to bleed, so that the vein does not move and fail when struck.  

Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;  
For there are veins that move like cords during bleeding, and there are some that are filled with air, so that when the lancet is applied, they retract, and the vein cannot be opened, and thus it happens with such veins.  

et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.  
And if the vein is opened, the wound may be too narrow; therefore, the bleeder must be cautious in these matters.  

Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;  
And if the vein opens the first time, it is good;  

se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.  
if not, then try again slightly below or above the spot quickly, as long as the area is not swollen.  

Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:  
And if the spot is swollen and the patient is alarmed, leave it for one or two days without binding the arm:  

par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;  
possibly hot abscesses may form there;  

ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;  
do not enter the bath, then resume the bleeding if the patient is willing;  

et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;  
and if the opening is small, or the blood flows thinly, and you fear not enough blood will come out, strike in the same opening directly with the lancet;  

et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;  
and open it slightly and quickly, before the area becomes swollen;  

car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.  
for this happens many times when the wound is small.  

Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;  
If you see the spot swell, do not resume the bleeding, and apply a bit of oil residue, for it soothes the flow of blood and is better in that spot than the oil itself;  

et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;  
and thus administer oil residue in each bloodletting when you bleed the veins, to stop the flow of blood;  

et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;  
and the same effect is achieved by theriac and ox balm when applied to the spot;  

si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.  
it refines and spreads the blood when it is too thick.  

Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;  
And if there appears a large abscess, which happens often, especially when it is not bled except at that time when the vein’s opening is small, hasten, and apply a sponge soaked in water and slightly warm salt, and press it for an hour;  

et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;  
and it is necessary to do this after the blood flows from the vein, and if some blackness or greenness remains at the site after a few days, it does no harm;  

et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.  
and if you wish, apply something of aloe or myrrh mixed in juice of calamint, pennyroyal, or the like.  

Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:  
And often there appears an abscess or swelling at the bleeding site of the basilica vein:  

met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.  
then place your hand on it, and if you find the site soft under the hand’s compression, this appearance is bad.  

Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;  
Avoid then applying anything we have mentioned, for there is a risk that arterial blood may flow;  

mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.  
but make a dry plaster to harden the site, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.  

Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.  
And draw blood from each according to the quantity of his strength and the color of the blood.  

Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;  
For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red;  

et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;  
and if you see it thick, let it flow until it becomes thinner;  

et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.  
and if it is too warm, let it cool down.  

Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;  
And for someone who is full-blooded and strong, and needs blood extraction, it is necessary to make a larger incision, and use wide lancets;  

et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;  
and for someone who is weak, do the opposite, and they must be bled little and often, and bleeding must be done by cutting across, not by piercing;  

et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.  
and this manner of bleeding is safe from blood leakage and nerve cutting, and is better than bleeding along or across.  

Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;  
And to the one whose body fails due to bloodletting, it is necessary to give bread moistened in pomegranate juice;  

s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII. Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.
if he is heated, then draw blood three or four times. And if he is of a cold complexion, let him eat before the bloodletting bread moistened in must syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, chickpeas, and a well-scented syrup.  

Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.  
And if he faints during the bloodletting, after the loss of much blood, it is necessary for him to sip meat broth and subtle aromatic syrup, and to use the other remedies that we have described in the section or chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of the vein.  

Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.  
And if he wishes to air his arm and bleed again, it is necessary, when he is weakened by heavy bloodletting, that he bleeds little by little, according to the measure of his ongoing strength.  

Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.  
And he who wishes to air his arm after the first bloodletting, and has a strong body, should bleed himself seven hours after the first bloodletting, or after the ninth hour.  

Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.  
And he who wishes to bleed another part should let blood on the second or third day.  

Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;  
For there is much blood in the body which is already heated, and it brings about fever;  

si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;  
thus it is necessary to draw a large quantity, and widen the incision until he falls into faintness;  

puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;  
then observe all the conditions of bloodletting, and place your hand on his pulse as he bleeds, so that death does not occur in place of fainting, as this happens often when the bloodletter is negligent;  

et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;  
and it is not proper, when you wish to untie the arm and let the blood flow a second time, and the incision is closed, to press strongly on it;  

ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;  
nor if the arm is bent, that he should extend it hastily, for that would be harmful;  

mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;  
but leave it until it bleeds a second time;  

ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.  
or prick it with the tip of the lancet, so that the blood which has coagulated in the vein exits outside, and apply a bit of salt dissolved in water, and press lightly on it.  

Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.  
And if the vein is swollen, then leave it and do not press on it, until the swelling subsides.  

Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.  
And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, then bleed in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.  

Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.  
The vein in the middle of the arm is bled in place of the head vein because it is connected.  

Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;  
And the method of bloodletting is such that the patient places his hand in hot water until the veins are red;  

puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;  
then bind it moderately so that the veins appear clearly, then bleed it across, not wide nor long;  

et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;  
and let the incision be wide, and let the blood be drawn near the joint of the hand, and if the blood cannot flow, then place the hand back in hot water and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough;  

et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;  
and if it is in summer, do not put the hand back in hot water, for it is done more in winter than in summer;  

et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.  
and the bloodletting from this vein is safer than from all other veins, as there is neither artery nor nerve there.  

Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:  
The bloodletting from the inner part of the right hand is beneficial for all liver diseases, and this is the method:  

estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;  
press the hand and place it in hot water until the vein is swollen so that it can be seen;  

et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;  
and bleed it across, and if you cut it completely, it does no harm;  

et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.  
and do not go too deep, for the nerves below are entirely bare of flesh, and then place the hand back in hot water if the blood has coagulated in the wound and cannot flow.  

Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.  
And when you have drawn as much blood as necessary, then apply oil and salt to the vein to heal it quickly, and do so for each vein.  

Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.  
The bloodletting from the left hand is beneficial for diseases of the spleen, and do exactly as I have described for the right side.  

Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.  
The bloodletting of the saphenous vein is beneficial for all diseases below the body, such as diseases of the womb, retention of menstrual flow, diseases of the kidneys, thighs, and chronic leg ailments, and similar conditions.  

Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;  
And the method of its bloodletting is that the patient places their foot in hot water and rubs the vein until it appears, then ties above the joint of the foot.  

et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;  
The vein is at the ankle, and many branches extend above the foot.  

saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.  
Bleed it then either on the larger branch or at the ankle, for it is very effective.  

Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;  
And if you bleed it on the foot, be careful of the nerves below, and bleed it across as though cutting.  

et soit li flaimes anesil.  
And let the lancet be rounded.  

Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.  
And if the blood cannot flow, place the foot back in the water and let the vein empty well.  

Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;  
And if the bloodletter misses the first time, try again a little higher, for the area is safe.  

ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.  
Do not fear the nerve, as we have said, and do the same for the saphenous vein of the other foot.  

Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.  
The location of the sciatic vein is at the outer ankle, and its bloodletting is effective for hip pain when it is caused by hot blood.  

Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;  
And the method of its bloodletting is that the patient enters a bath and presses four fingers above the ankle, twisting, for otherwise the vein does not appear.  

et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;  
And if it appears, bleed it in every way you can, cutting across.  

et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.  
And it is better to cut it, for the area is safe, and it is well known among many people.  

Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;  
And if you cannot find it, bleed one of its branches that appears on the top of the foot, near the little toe, and be careful of the nerves.  

et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;  
Let the blood flow as much as you want, then untie the binding, apply cotton, and press it.  

ele est maintenant sanee.  
It will heal immediately.  

Des sainies de ventouse  
On the bloodletting of cupping  

Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;  
Cups are made of horns, brass, or glass;  

et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:  
and cupping is done in two ways:  

ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.  
either by striking and drawing blood or without striking.  

Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:  
And this cupping without striking is done in two ways:  

ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;  
either with fire or without fire.  

et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;  
And cupping, which is done by striking and drawing blood, is performed in fourteen places on the body, one of which is on the crown of the head;  

et li autres est emmi le col;  
another is in the middle of the neck;  

et II autres en II costeis dou col;  
and two others are on the sides of the neck;  

et li ventouse desoz lou menton;  
and a cup below the chin;  

et li ventouse des II espaules;  
and cups on the two shoulders;  

et li ventouse sus les crupies;  
and cups on the buttocks;  

et les ventouses emmi les II bras;  
and cups in the middle of the two arms;  

et les ventouses des II jambes;  
and cups on the two legs;  

et les ventouses des II chevilles;  
and cups on the two ankles;  

et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;  
and cupping does not draw much blood, except from small veins scattered in the flesh, and thus it does not weaken the body as vein bloodletting does.  

et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.  
And it is not appropriate for it to be applied, whether with fire or without, in any disease caused by overfullness, until the entire body is emptied.  

Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;  
And if cupping is necessary due to disease or custom, it should be applied at any time at the beginning of the month, at the end, in the middle, or at any time.  

car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;  
For there are those who, when they need cupping, have a heavy head;  

et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;  
and there are those who find fullness and redness in their face, head, and neck, and dimness in their eyes;  

et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;  
and those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, have a swollen tongue, and spit blood;  

et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.  
and there are those who dream and see blood, wounded people, corpses, and similar things at night.  

Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.  
And when we see these signs, especially in the middle of the month, we recommend cupping after three hours of the day.  

Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;  
Bloodletting from the basilic vein helps with head pains that come to the eyes, and it is not necessary for this to follow a complete evacuation of the body.  

et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;  
And this cupping serves in place of the cephalic vein bloodletting, and it is not suitable for those of a cold complexion or those who have catarrh, as it greatly harms them.  

et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.  
And thus it is not appropriate for elderly people or those with cold diseases in the head to use it.  

Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.  
And he who bleeds himself often becomes forgetful, and therefore it is necessary to place the cupping glass a little lower, for fear of forgetfulness.  

Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;  
The cupping at the middle of the neck serves in place of bloodletting from the head and basilic vein, and thus it is effective for constriction of the chest, splitting of the lung canal, cough, and fullness.  

et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.
