And it must be applied lightly, for if it grips too firmly, it causes forgetfulness or distress in the stomach and heart.  

Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;  
The cupping on the two sides of the neck is effective for head pain, ophthalmia, migraine, strangulation, and pain at the roots of the teeth, and serves in place of bloodletting from the basilic vein.  

et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.  
And you must instruct the healer to press with his hand when applying it, so that he does not cut an artery and cause a flow of blood.  

Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;  
The cupping below the chin is effective for mouth diseases, gum decay, and similar conditions affecting the mouth.  

et est en leu des sainies des II levres.  
And it serves in place of bloodletting from the two lips.  

Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.  
The cupping on the shoulders is effective for diseases caused by heat and fullness.  

Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;  
The cupping on the elbows is as effective as that on the three veins of the arm, as it draws blood from these large veins.  

et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.  
And instruct the healer not to strike too deeply, for the place is bare of flesh and lies over nerves and arteries.  

Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;  
The cupping glass applied to the lower back is effective for hemorrhoids of the rectum and diseases beneath it, and the cupping glass must be large and made of brass, as it needs to draw well.  

et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;  
And perchance, if it were delicate, it would break.  

et i fai grans plaies.  
And it causes large wounds.  

Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;  
The cupping on the legs openly lets blood, as it draws blood from the entire body, and is effective for chronic pains in the loins, womb, and bladder, and eases menstruation.  

et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.  
And they serve in place of the two saphenous veins and the two ankles, yet they weaken the body after long use and cause fainting in many cases.  

Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;  
The manner of applying the cupping glass is that you first place it empty, suck moderately, and set it quickly, moving it evenly, and not ceasing until you see the place redden and swell, and the redness of the blood appear.  

puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:  
Then strike, reapply the cupping glass, and take heed of the body's condition, for there are those who have tender flesh and open pores.  

si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;  
In such cases, it is necessary to strike only once, and to make large and somewhat deep wounds.  

et suce legierement.  
And suck lightly.  

Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:  
And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to strike twice.  

la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.  
The first time to refine the pathway of the thick blood.  

Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;  
And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to strike a third time.  

et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.  
And when we wish to draw blood little by little, once is sufficient.  

Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;  
And if we wish to draw a lot of blood, we repeat often.  

et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:  
And if the blood is thick, strike deeply, and the limit is when the skin is pierced suddenly, and for one with thick and tough skin and narrow pores, you must anoint the cupping sites with opening and dissolving oils.  

se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;  
If it is in summer, use oil of violet, sweet almond oil, or oil of gourd seed.  

et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.  
And if it is in winter, use oil of watercress, lily, chamomile, or similar.  

Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.  
And if the superfluity is thick and cold, take oil of amaranth, balsamite, dill oil, or similar.  

Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.  
And if the one being bled has tender flesh and wide pores, no oil is needed, but they must be washed after cupping with rose water, cold water, nightshade water, gourd water, purslane water, or similar.  

Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.  
And one who has much moisture should rise with water of myrtle, sumac, or similar substances.  

Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;  
And those who have thick superfluities rise with old wine, or elder water, or a decoction of dill or chamomile, or other similar substances.  

et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;  
And it is not advisable to perform cupping before or during a bath, but rather an hour or two afterward.  

et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.  
And one must not sleep after cupping, and it is necessary to take precautions when one is about to be cupped and after being cupped.  

Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;  
And beware if the person being bled is choleric, and if the blood is too sharp and inflamed.  

si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;  
Then they must take cold things, such as pomegranates, endives, lettuce with vinegar, and similar items.  

et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.  
And they should eat young chickens, capon meat, and moist foods.  

Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;  
And one with a cold complexion should take honey syrup and aromatic medium wine, which is between old and new, eat little, and consume young chickens, small birds, and pigeons.  

et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;  
And on the day they are cupped, they should drink more than eat.  

et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;  
And it is sometimes necessary to give certain men treacle or nutmeg before or after cupping to strengthen the principal organs.  

et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.  
And the blood should be refined, but those who are hot in nature must not drink it.  

Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;  
The cupping glasses applied without incision are those placed on the liver, the spleen, the gouty joint, the stomach, the abdomen, the loins, and the hip, because these parts do not tolerate being struck upon. And they are only applied to draw blood from one part to another, such as placing them on the breasts when the nose bleeds.  

por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;  
To remove the viscosity in a part, as when we place cupping glasses on the stomach and abdomen to reduce the organ's size.  

et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;  
And it removes pain when there is obstruction or stone, and by its attractive power, it may remove the obstruction or dislodge the stone from its place.  

et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;  
And it acts similarly when applied to the liver and spleen when there is retained flatulence, and these cupping glasses are applied empty only to suck.  

et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.  
And sometimes they are applied with fire, and other times filled with hot water, as in pleurisy, and in such cases, the cupping glass is filled with plain hot water or water in which appropriate herbs have been cooked.  

Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:  
The form of the cupping glass applied with fire is as follows:  

Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;  
It should be two fingers wide and half a palm deep, and on the side around the middle, it should have a small hole, as if for inserting a needle, and it should be made of brass, smooth at the front so as not to injure the patient when placed on the body.  

et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;  
And in the middle, it should have a transverse rod of brass or iron for placing a lit candle, and they should come in large and small sizes depending on the illness and the age of the person receiving them.  

car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.  
For the cupping glasses for children differ from those for the elderly, and those for the thin differ from those for the fat.  

Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:  
And this is how this cupping glass should be placed on the body:  

empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;  
Take a wax candle or a wick, and place it in the center of the cupping glass across the rod in the middle, so that the flame is at the bottom of the glass and does not burn the patient.  

et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;  
Then place it on the body, and your fingers should cover the hole we mentioned, so that when desired, the vapor escapes, and the cupping glass is removed.  

et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.  
And take the wick again as before, and repeat often if necessary.  

En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;  
In the cupping glass applied for pleurisy, with water, there is neither rod nor hole, and it is only applied when filled with water and placed directly on the body.  

et c’est li forme:  
And this is the form:  

Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;  
Leeches are only applied to parts where cupping cannot be used due to their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places.  

et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;  
and to places devoid of flesh, such as fingers or the nose, and similar areas.  

et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;  
And the method for their use is as follows: when you find leeches in clean fresh waters, free from decay, take them;  

et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;  
and place them in fresh water for a night so they become accustomed and have nothing in their stomachs;  

et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;  
then let the vein be bled and cupped, rub the area until it is red, and apply the leeches;  

et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.  
and when they are full and fall off, if it is a place where a cup can be applied, apply it, for it is very beneficial afterward.  

Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;  
If not, cleanse the area with garlic and then with water thoroughly, and then compress it;  

et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;  
and if the spot bleeds too much after the leeches, wet a linen cloth in cold water and place it on the area until the bleeding stops;  

et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;  
and if the bleeding persists, apply powdered vitriol, galls, or similar substances until it stops;  

ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;  
or place halves of peeled beans on the area and leave them until they adhere to the spot, and it will stop immediately;  

et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.  
and if you need more, take other leeches.  

Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;  
And if the leeches do not attach, rub the spot with fresh blood, or prick it with a needle until blood flows, then apply the leeches, and as soon as they sense the blood, they will adhere;  

et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.  
and when you want them to fall off, sprinkle a bit of powdered aloe and salt, or ashes, on them, and they will immediately let go.  

Ci comence li livre des brisures  
Here begins the book of fractures.  

Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.  
This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, as it concerns the restoration of fractures and dislocations.  

Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;  
Know, dear son, that foolish physicians abandon this chapter, as they have never seen any of the ancient books nor read a single letter of them;  

et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;  
and for this reason, knowledge is scarce in our land, for I never found a single good one;  

et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;  
and I know nothing except through the knowledge of the ancient books, in which I have studied so much that I have drawn knowledge from them, through experimentation, and through the habits of my life;  

et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.  
and I have here described to you in this chapter what is contained within, and I have summarized it at the end, and I have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, as I have done in the two chapters before this.  

Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.  
It is fitting, then, that we speak in the prologue of this book about the summary of the discourse and the chapters where the wise focus their understanding and dwell on the truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.  

Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;  
I say that when a fracture, dislocation, twist, or break occurs in someone, you must hurry to bleed the patient on one side and the other, unless something prevents it, such as bodily weakness, being a child, or being elderly;  

ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;  
or if the weather is not very hot or too cold;  

et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;  
and eat cooling foods, such as cold broths, bird meat, and goat meat, and avoid drinking wine, eating fatty meats, or overfilling oneself with foods that fill the veins with blood, so that you do not risk a hot abscess or the spreading of matter to the limb;  

si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.  
so let the patient return to their original regimen that they had been following.  

Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.  
And when the broken bone begins to heal, the patient should be nourished with foods that provide substantial nourishment and contain viscosity, such as wheat cooked in water, rice, heads, feet, cow tripe, eggs, fresh fish, strong wine, and similar things.  

Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.  
For with such nourishment, fractures heal more thoroughly and quickly.  

Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;  
And know that the broken bones of the old and decrepit cannot heal or fuse well by their nature due to the dryness of their limbs, nor can those that are too tender, such as the bones of small children;  

mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;  
but do not worry, place a large tendon over the broken bone, which adheres and joins the limb together until it strengthens as it was before;  

et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.  
and do not impede its healing, and for this, the patient must be nourished with substantial foods, as we have mentioned.  

Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.  
And know that fractures vary in many ways.  

Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.  
For a fracture of the head is different from one of the chest or leg, and I will explain all kinds of fractures in this chapter.  

Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.  
For there is a fracture that radiates outward, and another sharp one, like the cut of a pen for writing.  

Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.  
And there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with only a small crack.  

Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;  
And each type requires its own technique and proper instrument for restoration, according to what the case demands.  

et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;  
A bone fracture is recognized when the area is twisted, visibly deformed, and makes a sound under the pressure of the hand;  

et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;  
and when there is no twisting or sound upon touch, and the patient feels no great pain, then there is no fracture;  

mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.  
but there may well be twisting, a crack, or a small fracture.  

Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.  
In such cases, do not manipulate it by hand, but apply the remedies mentioned later, and then gently bind it immediately.  

Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;  
And know that a fracture that radiates outward, where the two parts are disjointed, must immediately be aligned properly before a hot abscess forms there;  

et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;  
and if a hot abscess does form, let it be for a few days until the abscess subsides;  

puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;  
then set it evenly as best as you can, gently and wisely, and know that its healing will be easier than that of one with fragments;  

puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.  
then bind it as is appropriate, as will be explained later.  

Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;  
And if the bone is broken into pieces, stretch it on both sides, whether it is a hand or foot, using your hand if it is a small limb, or with two cords, or a cord and your hand.  

et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;  
And place the limb in its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken limb are separated, carefully return all the fragments to their places as best as you can, and ensure that your work does not cause the patient injury or pain.  

et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.  
And properly align the two ends of the bones in the best possible way.  

Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:  
And feel it carefully with your hand to determine if it seems not to be well-set:  

si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.  
then adjust it gently, and do not bind it too tightly, nor press it excessively as those do who, through their work, cause hot abscesses and contraction in the limb, as we have often seen.  

Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;  
And when the limb is properly set, instruct the patient well not to move it, whether awake or asleep, or when turning, or in any other way;  

et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.  
and ensure that the limb is so secure that the patient feels no pain.  

Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;  
For if they feel any pain, it is not properly set, and it must be adjusted so they feel no pain.  

et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;  
And be careful that it is set straight so that no deformity occurs when it is healed.  

et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.  
And the condition of the broken limb is as I have described to you.  

Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.  
Know that broken limbs vary in smallness, largeness, and shape.  

Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:  
For there are small members, such as arms and fingers and the like:  

si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;  
so they must be wrapped in soft and fine linen cloths;  

et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:  
and those which are large, such as the thigh and the leg:  

si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;  
must be wrapped with a wide and firm band, for the wide band embraces the entire large limb and compresses it evenly from all sides so that there is no defect;  

puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;  
then bind it around with light padding, three or four turns depending on the limb, and press gently with your hand on the band, then move above the fracture and compress it less, so that the fracture moves slightly away from itself;  

et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;  
and loosen the band little by little, until you cover a large part of the healthy area, then take another band and wrap it again over the fractured area;  

puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;  
then return to the area below the fracture and bind it moderately, neither too tightly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first binding above;  

puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.  
then place padding of linen or cloth between the bands until it is all even, then bind everything above with a bandage, and then place your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.  

Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;  
And if there is swelling or an abscess, then apply something to calm the hot abscess and to remove the swelling, and leave it so for a few days;  

puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:  
then bind over your splints, and let them be of the width of a split cane cut carefully, or of wood used for making baskets, or of palm branches, and shaped according to this design:  

mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;  
but the splint placed on the fracture must be slightly thicker and wider than the others;  

et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;  
and it must be as long as necessary for the limb, whether small or large;  

puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;  
then bind over the splints as you did in the first bandaging, then bind over it with a thread neatly, as in the first binding over the fracture;  

plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;  
the tighter it is at the top, the less so below;  

et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;  
and the thread must be moderate, neither too thick nor too fine, and made of soft linen;  

car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.  
for if the threads are thick, as I have seen in the work of fools who make their bindings from twisted linen cords, it is a great error, for the binding cannot be even if it is too fine, and there must not be less than the width of two fingers between each splint.  

Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.  
And if the patient is wounded by the edges of the splints after binding in healthy areas, place padding of linen or combed wool beneath them so that he is not injured.  

Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.  
When the wound is with the fracture and the bone is broken, I will describe its treatment hereafter.  

Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.  
And know that it is not necessary to bind all fractured limbs with splints on the first day.  

Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;  
For when the limb is large, splints should not be applied until after five or seven days, or more, depending on your certainty about preventing a hot abscess from occurring;  

et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:  
and here is the method of the ancients’ plasters to restore fractures, dislocations, and twists:  

et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.  
and it is that you take flour that sticks to the walls of the mill, and mix it with plenty of egg, and apply this preparation, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common method of the plaster that restores the fracture in various situations, and especially for women and small children, because it is neither too hot nor too cold.  

Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:  
Another method of plaster for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists:  

pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;  
take 3 ounces each of frankincense, ladanum, spikenard, asafetida, Arabic gum, and myrrh, 10 ounces of each;  

mirre et aloes, ana V З.;  
myrrh and aloes, 5 ounces each;  

alechil VIIII З.;  
rock alum, 9 ounces;  

et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;  
and make them into a powder and mix them with plenty of egg;  

se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.  
if the person’s complexion is warm, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, restores broken bones quickly, and is effective for many people.  

Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:  
Another method of plaster effective for twists:  

pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;  
take 10 ounces each of myrrh and marshmallow;  

mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;  
myrrh and aloes, 9 ounces each;  

acaice VI З.;  
acacia, 6 ounces;  

bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.  
Armenian bole, 10 ounces, and grind it well, mix it with water or plenty of egg, and apply it.  

Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:  
Another method of plaster for joints and bones displaced from their places, which soothes the resulting pain and prevents the fracture from worsening:  

pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.  
take fresh wool, soak it in oil cooked with garlic, and apply it to the area.  

Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.  
This plaster does not restore, but it is good for calming a hot abscess and properly removing pain.  

Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:  
Another method of plaster that restores broken bones:  

pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.  
Take dried fig leaves and ground ivy leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster.  

Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.  
Another method of plaster for restoring bone fractures and reducing the remnants of the abscess.  

Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;  
Take root of marshmallow, chamomile, violet flowers, and vetch flour, one part of each;  

et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.  
and grind them, mix with wine, and if the limb is inflamed, mix it with moist coriander water or plain water, and use it.  

Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.  
Another method of plaster, stronger than the first, when a hard abscess appears during the restoration of the limb.  

Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;  
Take roots of marshmallow, linseed, pomegranate flower, melilot, and elder, and flowers of violets and chamomile, all in equal parts;  

et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.  
and grind them, mix with saline water, or plain water, or wine, depending on the heat of the limb and its condition.  

Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.  
Hippocrates says in his book that nothing should be placed on a fractured limb for restoration except a cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and says it should be neither too soft nor too hard.  

Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.  
And Galen believes that for restoring a fractured limb, slightly warm dry substances should be applied, such as myrrh, aloes, incense, and similar things, as we have described.  

Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:  
Another method of plaster that is effective for wounds and pain:  

pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.  
Take myrrh, human hair cut into pieces, or bird feathers, and marshmallow, and salt in equal parts, grind them, and make a plaster and apply it.  

Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;  
And then loosen it a little later, and check whether the patient feels any pain or if the bone has moved from its place;  

si ne lou deslie par mains jors.  
if not, do not loosen it for several days.  

Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;  
And if pain occurs in the area, or itching, restlessness, or swelling, act quickly, loosen it, and immediately remove the plaster;  

et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;  
and take light cloth, a moistened sea sponge, and dip it in water, and cleanse the area until the itching ceases and the pain is soothed;  

puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;  
then let the limb rest for an hour, then apply dry wool soaked in water or rose oil, and bind it for one night until you are certain of the absence of a hot abscess;  

et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;  
and let the inflammation of the limb subside, and the pain be removed, then restart the gentle binding and apply a little plaster, and do not bind it as tightly as before;  

et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.  
and proceed carefully until it is healed.  

Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.  
And if you see that the hot abscess, redness, pain, and swelling are entirely gone, and you need plaster and binding, then restart it as you did before, evenly.  

Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;  
And if none of the issues we mentioned arise in the limb, do not loosen it until after three, four, five, or seven days;  

et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;  
and sometimes leave it for twenty days, depending on what you observe, until the fracture solidifies and the flesh begins to close over it;  

adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;  
then bind it more tightly than before, and nourish it well, as I have previously explained;  

et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;  
and if you see the area drying out more than necessary, know that nourishment cannot reach it;  

arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;  
then moisten it with warm lukewarm water each time you loosen it, and do this every third day, and slightly loosen the binding;  

par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:  
by this process, nourishment will flow to the limb, and it will heal quickly, avoiding the mistakes of foolish physicians who restore the limb improperly:  

c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.  
this is harmful, and such practices are dangerous, and I see no better method than to leave it and treat it properly.  

des diverses manieres de brisure  
Of the various types of fractures  

Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;  
There are many types of fractures, with various shapes, and their causes are distinct;  

car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;  
for there are fractures caused by the blow of a sword, where the strike removes all the bone down to the membrane beneath it, as an axe does to wood;  

et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».  
and for this reason, this type of fracture is called "hatching."  

Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;  
Or when the sword cuts the bone from above without piercing it, this type of fracture is called "simple."  

et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.  
And the wounds from these two fractures may be large or small.  

Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.  
And if there is a crushing impact, or a splitting, or a blow from a stone, or from falling on a stone, or other similar causes.  

Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.  
And if there is a piercing fracture that reaches the membrane beneath the bone, or that is above the bone, the wound may be either large or small.  

Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;  
And there is a wound that appears on the bone as fine as a hair, and the split is small, and for this reason, this fracture is called "capillary."  

et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;  
And if the wound is caused by being struck with a stone, or by falling, or by a similar occurrence, and a piece of bone is driven inward, the spot becomes hollowed, as when cauldron-makers strike on cauldrons;  

si entre li piere dedens.  
so the piece of bone enters within.  

Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;  
And this happens more often to those who have soft bones in the head, such as a child’s head;  

et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;  
and in all these types of fractures, small fragments of bone are detached like splinters;  

et je em parlerai en son leu.  
and I will speak of them in their proper place.  

Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.  
And we recognize all types of fractures by the signs above them, by probing with tents, and by the corrupted flesh that is over them.  

Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.  
The capillary type is known by this: when the bone is uncovered and one rubs it, the fracture appears black.  

En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.  
In treating a fracture, pay attention to the patient's symptoms, and if you see any adverse signs such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, convulsions, fainting, acute fever, bulging and reddening of the eyes, or other similar signs in various manifestations, then recovery is unlikely.  

Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.  
But if you see no alarming symptoms and hope for recovery, then begin the treatment.  

Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.  
And when the wounded comes first to you, and it is winter, you must remove the bone before the fourteenth day at the latest that you can.  

Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.  
And if it is summer, hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, before the membrane beneath the bone becomes corrupted, and the complications we have described occur.  

Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:  
And if the fracture of the bone reaches the membrane that covers the brain, you must incise the fractured part in this way:  

et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;  
and take the head of the wounded patient, and expose the bone in every way you can, especially around the shape of the wound as gently as you can, and if there is a flow of blood when the bone is exposed, or a hot abscess, aid it with what is necessary, which is to fill the area with cloths soaked in rose oil;  

et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;  
and let the wound rest until the hot abscess has subsided, and you are assured there is no flow of blood;  

puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:  
then begin to remove the bone around it, and this is done according to two methods of procedure:  

l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:  
the first method is that you make a narrow incision at the front, and this is its shape:  

Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.  
And then insert another incision larger than the first.  

Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;  
And the second method is to have a number of various incisions, some narrow and others wide, pointed, and made of Indian steel;  

et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.  
and work lightly so that you do not injure the head.  

Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;  
And if the bone is strong and hard, you must pierce around it before making incisions with augers, not too deeply so that they do not go beyond the bone of the skull, and there must be a margin or a ring at the tip to prevent the point from passing beyond the bone;  

et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;  
and you must have several, so that each matches the thickness of the bone, and so that you have augers for every type of skull;  

et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:  
and this is the shape of the three types of augers:  

Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;  
The technique for piercing around the fractured bone is that you place an auger on the bone and turn it with your fingers until you know the bone is pierced;  

puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;  
then place the auger in another spot a little farther, and do so all around, then cut with incisors the space of the bone that lies between the holes, and do this as delicately as you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you remove the bone with your hand or with one of the instruments you have, such as pliers or pincers;  

et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.  
and take care not to touch the brain or the membrane.  

Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;  
And when you have pierced and removed the bone, you must remove the remaining fragments of the bone with another instrument resembling an incisor, but it must be thinner and more delicate than the other incisors;  

et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;  
and if any small bones or fragments remain, remove them gently with one of the instruments;  

puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.  
then treat the wound with tents and ointments as we have described.  

Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;  
And the other method of procedure is the one Galen describes, which is safer;  

et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.  
and he greatly praised it, and this is what he said.  

Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:  
You must first expose a part of the bone, where the fracture is clearly visible, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will place beneath the head this lenticular incisor, whose shape is as follows:  

Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;  
And it does not cut on one side, but the blade is sharp on two sides, so that the cutting edge is directed toward the bone;  

puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;  
then strike lightly with a small mallet so that you cut the bone gently all around, and be very careful of the membrane beneath it;  

s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.  
if it is adhered to the bone, remove it gently, as it can be removed without harm and without fear.  

Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.  
And if the fracture of the bone does not reach the membrane, and the bone is only cut on the surface, and there are small pieces, you must smooth out the roughness and remove the splinters with a fine rasp, of which you should have various sizes to apply to each area in the most suitable way, depending on the procedure and the shape of the fracture.  

Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.  
Begin first with large rasps, then with finer ones, and do not stop until it is done properly.  

En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;  
In each of the other capillary incisions and subtle fractures, you must proceed according to their alignment;  

et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.  
and this is not difficult for someone who has devoted their study to this art.  

Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;  
And if the membrane is exposed, you must take a linen cloth, sized according to the wound, soak it in rose oil, and place it on the wound;  

puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;  
then take another cloth folded in two or three layers, soak it in wine and rose oil, and place it over the first cloth;  

et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;  
and do this as gently as you can so as not to harm the membrane, then apply another bandage over it, and do not tighten it further than what is needed to secure the wound only;  

et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;  
and leave it like this for one or two days until the hot abscess has subsided, then loosen it and apply medicines such as lily roots, vetch flour, frankincense powder, aristolochia, and similar things;  

et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;  
and make a powder from these things, place it on the wound, and always apply cleansing medicines without irritation;  

et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;  
and ensure that the wound is always clean, leaving no ointment on it nor allowing dirt to accumulate, for when dirt gathers on the brain’s membrane, it corrodes and rots it, causing great harm to the patient;  

car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.  
for when something irritating is applied to the membrane, it causes contraction above.  

Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.  
Take care, therefore, that if any bad complications occur to the patient, as we have described, it is truly dangerous without a doubt.  

Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;  
And if discoloration appears only because of the medicine applied, having such a property, you must take one part honey and three parts rose oil, soak a cloth in it, and place it on the membrane;  

puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.  
then treat it in the necessary ways until it is healed.  

Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;  
Know that sometimes both upper parts of the nose are fractured, or only one of them, because these are two bones;  

et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.  
and the one below is cartilaginous and does not break but only swells or twists, and then heals.  

Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;  
And if one of the two parts is fractured, you must insert your little finger into the nostril and adjust the fracture from inside with your index finger and your thumb from outside, until the nose returns to its natural shape;  

et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.  
and do this gently, ensuring the patient does not feel pain from your procedure.  

Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.  
And if the fracture is in the upper part of the nose and the finger cannot reach the spot, you must align it using the end of a slightly thick rod.  

Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;  
And if the fracture is on both sides, do the same, and hurry to set it on the first day, if possible;  

se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.  
if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the hot abscess has subsided, then place linen tents at the tip of the nose, if the fracture is on one side.  

Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;  
Or insert another on the other side if the fracture is there;  

et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.  
and the tents should be thick enough to fill the nostrils.  

Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.  
And some restorers said the tents should be soaked in butter and changed daily.  

Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;  
It does not seem right to me, but rather they should be soaked in a mixture of egg white and powdered saffron;  

puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.  
then leave the tent in place until the bone is firm and the cartilage has hardened.  

Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;  
And sometimes goose feathers are placed in the nose instead of tents, wrapped in a soft cloth, to hold the fracture, and the patient breathes through them;  

or fai lou kel ke tu vues.  
now do whichever you prefer.  

Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.  
And if a hot abscess appears on the nose while you are working on it, apply wax or cotton soaked in rose oil or a little diachylon ointment.  

Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;  
And if no hot abscess appears, apply an external plaster made of sesame flour and frankincense powder mixed with egg white, then place light tow on it and do not bind the nose tightly;  

et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;  
and if the nasal fracture is small and broken into tiny pieces, extract them with appropriate instruments, then sew the split and treat it with flesh-generating and healing substances, such as suitable plasters and ointments;  

et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.  
and if there is no wound inside the nose, treat it with tents, inserting small lead pipes until it is healed.  

de la routure de la mandibule
Of the fracture of the mandible  

Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.  
When the mandible is broken below, and there is no external wound, and the fracture is only external and not split in two, except for being slightly inwardly arched, one can recognize it easily.  

Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;  
If the fracture is on the right side, you must place your index finger inside the patient's mouth.  

et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.  
And if the fracture is in the left side of the mandible, then insert the index finger of your right hand, push the fracture inward gently, adjust it externally with the other hand, and make it even.  

Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.  
If the mandible fracture is separated into two parts, you must extend both sides until they are even.  

Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;  
If the teeth become loose or there is a fracture, bind them with a thread of gold, silver, or silk, then apply wax to the broken mandible and place a double layer of cloth over it.  

et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.  
Place over the cloth a well-made splint or an even piece of leather, long and wide according to the mandible, bind it as tightly as you can, and instruct the patient to rest and eat light foods.  

Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;  
If you see that the shape changes, untie it on the third day, then readjust what has shifted.  

et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;  
Apply a plaster made of mill powder mixed with plenty of egg or sesame flour after removing the wax.  

et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;  
Place light wool over the plaster, and if the plaster hardens and the patient’s condition does not change, leave it until they are healed.  

maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.  
Often, it heals within three weeks.  

Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.  
If a hot abscess forms, administer the treatment we have often described.  

Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;  
If there is both a fracture and a wound, check whether any piece of bone is detached.  

si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.  
Carefully remove it with suitable instruments.  

Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.  
If the wound is narrow, widen it with a flame according to your need.  

Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.  
Once you have removed all the pieces and none remain, sew the wound if it is large, and apply one of the appropriate plasters to generate flesh until it heals.  

de la forcele
Of the clavicle  

Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:  
The clavicle often breaks in front, toward the shoulder, and the fracture occurs in three ways:  

ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;  
Either it is broken and separated into two parts with fragments, which is the easiest to restore.  

ou il i a brisure avec plaie.  
Or there is a fracture with a wound.  

Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;  
When the fracture is without a wound, the process is that you have two assistants, one of whom holds the support for the broken clavicle.  

et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;  
And the other stretches the neck toward the affected side.  

puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.  
Then align the fracture with your fingers so that its shape is as it should be, with no projection or gap.  

Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;  
If you need to extend further, place under the patient’s shoulder a round ball of cloth or wool, as thick as needed.  

et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.  
Stretch and lift the clavicle, compressing the ball with your hand so that you align the fracture as required.  

Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.  
If you cannot draw out the end of the clavicle because it is too deep, the patient must lie often on their side, place a medium pillow under the shoulder, and have the assistant press the shoulder downward until the clavicle bone is raised.  

Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;  
Then adjust the fracture with your fingers, and if you find it shattered, you must make an incision above it.  

et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;  
Gently extract the fragments, and if the bone cannot align due to an overgrowth, cut it with one of the chisels you have.  

mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:  
However, you must place this instrument under the clavicle to protect the surrounding tissue.  

et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;  
It resembles a spoon but is not curved, and it should be as wide as needed, according to the size of the bone and the nature of the task.  

et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;  
It should have two ends, as you see, one wide and the other narrow, corresponding to the shape of the wound you made when extracting the bone.  

et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.  
When you are sure there is no hot abscess, sew the wound; if the fracture is small or you suspect a hot abscess, fill the wound with cloth strips and tents according to its size.  

Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.  
And if hot swellings appear there, moisten a cloth with rose oil, vinegar, and wine, and apply it.  

Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;  
The setting of the bone, when it is without wounds and without cuts, is to apply a plaster made of mill powder and egg white to the bone, place light wadding over it, and position a pad under the armpit, if necessary.  

Puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;  
Then take a very large bandage, about a palm wide, and place a double cloth over the wadding and the plaster.  

Puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;  
Then take a thin splint, three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage so that the ends of the bandage hang loose.  

Et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;  
Place the splint over the fracture, and wrap the bandage over the neck, under the healthy armpit, and under the injured armpit.  

Et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;  
Bring it back together from each side, and when you see that the binding holds the fracture properly, and you clearly see that the splint does not move on the fractured bone, check it each day, and if the binding loosens, tighten it again.  

Et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;  
Have the patient lie on their back, and when they sleep, place a small pillow under the armpit to raise the support upwards.  

Si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;  
This will relieve the fracture of the shoulder blade by aligning the shoulder, or you tie their arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless bad complications arise, for up to twenty days.  

Puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;  
Then renew the plaster if you see it is needed, tighten it, and leave it this way until it is healed.  

Et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.  
And it is healed within twenty-eight days at most, and sooner for some men.  

De la brisure de l’espaule  
On the fracture of the shoulder  

Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;  
It rarely happens that the shoulder is fractured at a wide place or in the middle, and it is not known except by touch.  

Si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;  
Align it according to the shape of the fracture, and restore it to its natural form in every way you can.  

Puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;  
Then place mill powder mixed with egg white on the area, along with light wadding, and apply a double cloth over it.  

Puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;  
Then place a broad, thin splint slightly wider than the shoulder, and if there are hollows beneath the splint in any part of the shoulder, fill those hollows with flax wadding so that the splint sits evenly.  

Et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;  
Then tighten it firmly with a large bandage so that the splint does not move from its place, and check the binding every day.  

Et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;  
Each time it loosens, tighten it, and realign the splint if it is out of place, and have the patient lie on their side.  

Et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.  
And the shoulder is healed in twenty or twenty-five days.  

Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.  
And when this time has passed, untie it, and be assured, for this is not a bone that is easily dislocated.  

Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.  
And if a piece of bone protrudes and presses under the skin, make an incision and remove it, and do what we have said about fractures of the shoulder blade to relieve hot swelling.  

De la brisure dou pis  
On the fracture of the chest  

Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;  
The chest is sometimes fractured in the middle, but this happens rarely.  

Mais il brise sovent au defuer.  
But it often fractures on the outside.  

Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.  
And when it is fractured in the middle, it collapses inward, and the patient feels great pain, has difficulty breathing, coughs, and may vomit blood, and the hollows in the fractured bone are visible and can be clearly felt.  

Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;  
The treatment is to have the patient lie often on their back, place a cushion between their shoulders, then press the shoulders and bring the ribs on both sides together with your hands, carefully adjusting them to align as perfectly as possible so that the shape of the bone is as it should be.  

Puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;  
Then apply plasters and wadding over a thin splint of willow or other light wood, wrap it in a cloth, and bind it over the fractured bone so that it does not move.  

Et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;  
Wrap the binding around the back, tighten it properly, and check the binding every hour; if it loosens, tighten it again.  

Et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;  
And if it must be untied due to irritation, itching, pain, or swelling at the site, untie it quickly, adjust the plaster, and address what has arisen with appropriate treatments.  

Puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.  
Then reapply the plaster and tighten it until it is healed.  

De la brisure des costes  
On the fracture of the ribs  

Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;  
Know that rib fractures only occur in the thicker parts near the back and at the inner ends, and they only break because they are brittle.  

Et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.  
This can be clearly felt through probing with the fingers.  

Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.  
The treatment is to align the fracture as it should be.  

Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.  
Then apply the plaster and secure it with a splint, if necessary.  

Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;  
If the rib fracture collapses inward, the patient feels great pain and a stabbing sensation, like pleurisy, because the bone pierces the membrane.  

Et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.  
They breathe with difficulty, cough, and vomit large quantities of blood, which is a grave condition, and the ancients devised great skill to address it.  

Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.  
Some say that food which bloats the belly should be administered to push the fracture outward.  

Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.  
We do not do this, lest hot swellings develop there, if they are not already present.  

Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.  
If they are present, treat them accordingly.  

Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;  
Some of them said that cupping should be applied to the area to suck forcefully, and this seems reasonable.  

Toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.  
However, there is a concern that cupping might draw impurities to the area due to its weakened state.  

Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.  
Some said the area should be covered with wool moistened in warm oil, and tents should be placed between the ribs to equalize the surrounding binding, then treated as for pleurisy with food and medicine.  

Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;  
If the patient feels such severe pain that they cannot bear it due to the bone piercing the membrane, and the patient is at risk, it is necessary to make an incision over the fractured rib and place an instrument underneath to protect the tissue.  

Et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.  
Then the bone should be cut and removed gently, the two edges of the wound sewn together if it is large, and treated with plasters until it heals.  

Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;  
If hot swellings occur, place cloths moistened with rose oil over the area.
