Et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.  
And treat the area as required for swellings, and have the patient lie frequently on the appropriate side until they are healed.  

De la brisure dou col  
On the fracture of the neck  

Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;  
Sometimes fractures occur in the bones of the neck, but they rarely bend.  

Et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.  
The same applies to the spine.  

Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.  
When this happens to someone and you want to know if they will recover, check if their hands are soft, swollen, and lifeless, and if they cannot move or extend them; when you prick them with a needle, they feel nothing.  

Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.  
Know that this condition is often fatal, but if they can move their hands and feel when they are pressed or pricked, know that the joints of the bone are intact, and the patient can recover if treated properly.  

Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;  
If a similar condition occurs in the spine, and you want to know if they will recover, check if the feet are soft and if the same symptoms appear as in the hands, and whether involuntary wind or bowel movements occur on the back.  

Et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.  
And when they are turned onto their stomach, observe if involuntary bowel movements happen.  

Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.  
And when they are turned onto their back and want to sit up, they cannot do so.  

Saiches qu’il est mortelz:  
Know that this condition is fatal.  

Si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.  
Do not exert yourself with treatment in such a case.  

Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.  
If these symptoms are absent, the condition is milder.  

Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;  
The treatment is to observe if there is a hot swelling, and apply rose oil or egg yolk oil to the spine until it subsides.  

Puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;  
Then apply one of the comforting and drying plasters, bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest.  

Et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.  
And ensure they do not sleep on the side where they feel pain until they are healed.  

Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;  
If any bone is displaced, it is necessary to cut over the area.  

Et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;  
Remove the bone, then bring together the two edges of the wound, if it is large, with stitching, and treat it with healing ointments until it is healed.  

Et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;  
If the head of the bone, called the "head of the spine," is fractured, insert your thumb of the left hand and align it as best as you can with the other hand, then apply the plaster and splint, if needed.  

Puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.  
Then secure it, and if there is a displaced bone, cut over it, remove it, and treat the wound until it is healed.  

de la brisure de l’os de la hainche  
On the fracture of the hip bone  

Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;  
It rarely happens that the hip bone is broken, and if it does, it is usually only a slight narrowing at the head.  

et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.  
It splits lengthwise, inclines inward, and causes the patient pain at the site, stinging, and swelling of the broken part.  

Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;  
The restoration consists of placing your hand on it until you are directly over the fracture.  

et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;  
And determine what the fracture is and its shape.  

et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.  
If the fracture is only at the head, align it so that it takes its natural shape.  

Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restoration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.  
If the fracture runs lengthwise or inclines inward, have the patient lie on their stomach until the restoration of the fracture is ready.  

Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;  
When you have aligned it, apply a plaster, then a splint of wood or leather, and bind the fracture tightly so it does not move.  

et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.  
And fill the area beneath the ribs until the level is even.  

Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.  
Instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side or on their back.  

Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;  
If a hot abscess develops, do not touch it until it subsides, and apply the treatment we mentioned earlier.  

et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;  
Then return to the restoration and bind it as needed, provided there is no adverse complication.  

et c’est li maniere.  
And this is the procedure.  

de la brisure de l’ajutoire  
On the fracture of the shoulder joint  

Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:  
The shoulder joint is what lies between the elbow and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, it must be restored using one of two methods:  

dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:  
The first is to take a wooden rod of medium thickness, shaped as follows:  

Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;  
Tie two cords at both ends, suspend it above, and seat the patient on a chair.  

puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;  
Then place the broken arm over the rod so that it reaches the armpit, with a curve of wood in the middle, and hang a weight from it or have the assistant pull downward.  

puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.  
Then the physician aligns the fracture with their hands until the break is restored as it should be.  

Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.  
The second method involves laying the patient on their back, tying their hand to their neck, and instructing two assistants—one to hold above the fracture and the other to hold below it with a cord, each pulling in their direction.  

Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.  
If you want the traction to be stronger, tighten a cord below and above the fracture, and have each assistant pull in their respective direction.  

Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;  
If the fracture is near the head of the shoulder, place one cord under the armpit and another near the elbow, below the fracture.  

et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;  
Similarly, if the fracture is near the elbow, a cord must be applied lightly without strain, until the fracture is aligned at the site and at the elbow.  

puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.  
Then align the fracture as needed and bind it, provided no hot abscess develops.  

Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;  
If a hot abscess develops, do not bind it for seven days; instead, apply wool soaked in vinegar and rose oil until the abscess subsides.  

puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;  
Then bind it, and the method for binding is to apply a plaster over the fracture, bring the arm close to the shoulder joint, and place your hand on the shoulder or chest.  

et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.  
Apply the bandage and bind over the joint and the arm, so the arm acts as a splint unless something prevents it, or the bone is not displaced.  

Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;  
If you fear the bone may move, use splints, placing a wider and stronger splint over the fracture, with a finger’s width of space between each splint, and ensure each splint extends three fingers’ width beyond the fracture on either side.  

puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.  
Then bind over the splints, as I described at the beginning of the chapter on fractures, tighter at the center and looser outward.  

Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;  
And if you see the placement of the splints and the binding, as we have said, at the time you restore the broken limb, and you fear a hot swelling, then leave it bound until the seventh day, as we have said;  

puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.  
then check every three days the binding, so that irritation or inflammation does not occur at the site, or that nourishment cannot reach the limb because it is too tight.  

Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.  
Adjust it, as we have said.  

Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;  
And if no such incidents occur, do not loosen it until after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on their back with their hands on their stomach.  

et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;  
And place underneath the support a cushion filled evenly with wool, and monitor each hour of the day or night that the alignment of the broken limb does not shift, or the bindings do not loosen.  

si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;  
Adjust it with the help of medicine, and give the patient the food we mentioned earlier, prepared in such a way that it is initially light.  

et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.  
And when they begin to recover, let it be more substantial.  

Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;  
And it is customary that the supports and the leg should be fully restored within forty days.  

et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  
And then it should be loosened, and baths and medicinal ointments should be applied to straighten the site.  

Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.  
And if the constriction is severe and swollen, delay loosening for fifty days or two months.  

de la brisure du bras  
On the fracture of the arm  

Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;  
The arm is composed of two bones, called the two "fossils," one of which is small, and it is the one that follows the thumb.  

et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;  
And the other is large, and it is the one beneath, towards the little finger.  

par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.  
Sometimes the large bone alone breaks, or the small one, and sometimes both together.  

Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;  
When the small bone is broken, the restoration is simple, as is the healing.  

et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.  
And when the large bone is broken, the healing is more difficult and more severe than when both are broken together.  

Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.  
If it is the small bone alone that is broken, it must be slightly extended and set evenly.  

Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;  
And if it is the large bone, it must be bound more tightly.  

et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;  
And extend it on a cushion, and hold the thumb of the hand higher than the others, and the little finger lower than the other fingers, and let the patient sit cross-legged on themselves, with a cushion in front of them, higher, so that the patient endures no strain.  

puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.  
Then the assistant stretches the arm at the lower part towards the hand or the binding, and another assistant does the same above.  

Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.  
And then the physician sets it evenly, according to its best form.  

Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.  
And if the fracture has fragments, place each one in its position, and if there is any displaced one that pricks the flesh and you cannot restore it to its position, then cut and remove it, as we have said earlier.  

Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;  
And if the fracture has a wound, I have discussed this in the separate chapter.  

si pren la cure.  
Then undertake the treatment.  

Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;  
And if, at the beginning of the restoration, hot swelling occurs, apply a cloth smeared with cerate made from rose oil and white wax, that is neither too hard nor too soft.  

et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.  
And bind the cloth above it carefully, until the hot swelling is soothed.  

Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, puis met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;  
Then remove the cerate, and apply a plaster of mill powder mixed with plenty of egg, then place the splints, and let the splint on the fracture be always stronger and slightly wider than the others.  

et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:  
And know that there must be six splints on the arm in various positions.  

soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;  
Whether the fracture is in one bone or in both.  

et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;  
And tighten more on the fracture than elsewhere, and always less as you move away, as I said at the beginning of the chapter.  

et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;  
And let the cloths on the fracture be soft and moist, and not hard or rough.  

et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.  
And let the thread used for binding be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.  

Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.  
And check the limb and the binding after a few days.  

Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;  
And if any bad incidents occur to the limb, such as itching that affects it, you must bathe the limb with warm water until the itching is soothed;  

et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.  
and let the limb rest, not too tightly bound.  

Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.  
Then reapply the binding, and if the binding has loosened and the bone is displaced, or similar issues arise, adjust it.  

Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.  
And if you notice that nourishment cannot reach the limb because it is too tightly bound, you must loosen it slightly and leave it for a few days, until nourishment flows, and then tighten it again.  

Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.  
And if none of these issues occur with the patient, do not loosen it for twenty days.  

ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;  
Or thereabouts, then hang their hands at their neck, and let their shoulders be even, and ensure they avoid movement or dislocation, and let them sleep on their back.  

et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.  
And know that this fracture is restored in thirty or thirty-five days, and perhaps in twenty days, depending on the structure and the constitution of the patient.  

de la brisure de la main  
On the fracture of the hand  

Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.  
Know that fractures rarely occur on the back of the hand or at the joints of the fingers, and instead there are often dislocations.  

Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;  
And when the palm of the hand is broken or dislocated, the patient must sit cross-legged and sit upright, evenly before them.  

puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;  
Then place their hand stretched out on a cloth, and the assistant extends the broken bones, and the physician sets them evenly until they are well joined.  

et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;  
And apply the plaster and lint, if there is no swelling, then place a splint according to the size of the area.  

et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.  
And wrap it in a linen cloth.  

Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;  
And if the fracture is on the inner side around the palm, make a roll of cloths, and instruct the patient to press it against their broken palm.  

et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.  
And then bind it with a long cloth, and let the splint be of soft wood, as large as the palm of the hand, and tighten it as needed.  

Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.  
And if the fracture is on the outer side, you must place one splint above and another below on the palm, so that the hand remains open and straight, then wrap it entirely around the hand, and secure the binding between the fingers.  

Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;  
And if the fracture occurs at one of the finger joints, if it is the thumb, set it straight as required.  

et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;  
And bind it with the palm, and if you wish, place a small straight splint to support the fracture and prevent it from moving.  

et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;  
And if the fracture is in one of the other fingers, such as the index finger or another, set it straight and bind it with the healthy finger next to it.  

ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;  
Or bind them all together in one bundle, which is often better, or place a splint, as with the thumb.  

et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.  
And take care during the restoration and in managing hot swelling, and treat it as I have said.  

de la cuixe brisie  
On the fractured thigh  

Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;  
The bone of the thigh is often fractured, and it is evident when it turns forward or backward.  

et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.  
And the restoration is done by binding one strap above the fracture and another below.  

Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;  
And the patient lies on their back, and each assistant stretches their strap evenly on their side.  

et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.  
And this is when the fracture is in the middle of the bone.  

Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.  
And if the fracture is near the base of the thigh, one strap should be near the hip, and the other below the fracture.  

Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;  
And likewise, if it is near the knee, then the strap should be beside the knee, and the extension downward.  

puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.  
Then the physician sets the bone evenly with both hands until it is in its natural shape, then applies a plaster and binds it, if there is no hot swelling.  

Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;  
And if there is hot swelling, let it subside, then return to your work and treatment.  

li lieure est faite en teil maniere.  
The binding is done in this manner.  

Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;  
It is necessary that you wrap over the fracture a hard bandage folded two or three times, and leave the excess, then turn the leg so that the heel reaches the root of the buttock, and place a long thread between the thigh and the leg, below near the knee, with the ends of the thread coming out above;  

puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;  
then wrap the bandage over the leg and the thigh, then place splints on the fracture, and put one splint on the bone of the leg;  

puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;  
then fill the empty space between the leg and the thigh with soft cloths to ensure even pressure, then begin to tie tightly three or four twists over the fracture;  

et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;  
and the higher you go above the fracture, the less tightly you bind;  

puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;  
then attend to the two ends of the thread that you placed between the leg and the thigh, and tie to them the three splints that are above, then return below to the end of the thread, until you reach near the foot;  

et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.  
and tighten it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus, provided that no abscess, swelling, or other appearance occurs.  

Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;  
And if it occurs, then untie it and address what appears, as we have said many times;  

et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;  
and if there are pieces of bone that protrude, they must be removed, if possible;  

et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;  
and if this is not possible, then the area must be opened, and the piece extracted;  

et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.  
and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.  

Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;  
And sometimes the thigh is fractured in such a way that splints are applied to it, as is done for the forearm or the arm;  

toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.  
nevertheless, with the restoration done in this way, the patient does not limp.  

Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.  
And know that the thigh is restored in fifty days, or a little less or a little more, depending on the differences in constitutions.  

de la ruelle dou genoil  
Concerning the hollow of the knee  

Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.  
Know that fractures rarely occur in the hollow of the knee, but it bends often.  

Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.  
And if it fractures, it is only a crack or a perforation, and it occurs either with a wound or without a wound, and this is easily felt.  

Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;  
And the restoration is done by aligning what is dislocated to its proper place as much as possible;  

puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;  
then apply the plaster, and place a rounded splint if needed, and tighten it as required, then revisit all the measures we mentioned for other fractures, such as abscesses, heat, and other signs;  

si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.  
and apply the appropriate treatment for each condition, until it is healed.  

de la brisure de la jambe  
Concerning the fracture of the leg  

Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;  
Know that the leg contains two bones, one of which is rightfully called "mustel" and the other "foscile";  

et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.  Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.  
and the fractures occur in the same way as in the arm, and for this reason, the restoration is the same as for the arm, and the process is identical.  And if both bones are fractured together, the leg bends in all directions. 

Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.  
And if the smaller bone is fractured, it bends forward.  

Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;  
And if the larger bone is fractured, great pain is felt, and it is clearly visible;  

et torne desoz.  
and it bends downward.  

Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;  
Then perform extension, set it straight, and tie the splints evenly;  

mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;  
but nevertheless, if the fracture is severe and there are many fragments, the extension must be less and gentler;  

et l’alige selonc ta vertu.  
and adjust it according to your ability.  

Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;  
And when you have completed your work, take two wooden slats that enclose the leg on both sides, and are as long as the leg from the knee to below;  

puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;  
then wrap a bandage in two places above and below, and tie it in the middle as well, and at this point the leg cannot bend to the right or the left, and thus it is well secured;  

et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;  
and some apply a rod along the length of the leg, made of wood, and the leg is placed on it to prevent movement, and this is specifically done in fractures with a wound;  

et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;  
and the leg is moved each day to check for any abscess, heat, or other condition;  

si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.  
and treat it until it is healed.  

de la brisure des os dou piet  
Concerning the fracture of the bones of the foot  

A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.  
At the ankle, fractures do not occur, but sometimes fractures occur in the bones of the foot, and rarely in the toes, and they are usually simple cracks in various positions.  

Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;  
And if a fracture occurs in the bones of the foot, and you see these bones overlapping one another, have the patient place their foot on the ground as if they were trying to walk, then immediately place your foot on theirs, where the bones are raised, and press until they return to their places;  

puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.  
then apply plaster and padding, and place under the sole of the foot a small board with two flat ends, then bind it to the foot appropriately, after wrapping with cloths and other necessary materials.  

Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.  
And after three or four days have passed, untie the binding, for you will find the bones aligned, whether fractured or dislocated.  

Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;  
And if any toes are fractured, restore them as we have described for the fingers of the hand;  

puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;  
then place on the fractured toe a splint matching the length of the toe, and slightly wider, then place under the foot the board I mentioned, and tighten it appropriately;  

et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;  
and if two or three, or more, are fractured, place a splint on each toe according to its size, wrapped in a linen cloth, and tighten the board under the foot;  

et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.  
and let the end of the board extend beyond the sole of the foot, so that it holds it securely.  

Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;  
And you must not forget the other measures I mentioned for other fractures, as we have described;  

et secor chescun accident si com il covient.  
and address each complication as required.  

de la brisure de l’os dou poignil  
Concerning the fracture of the bone of the wrist  

Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;  
When the bone of a woman’s genital region is fractured, make her sit with her legs apart, then incline her toward her back, and have her held from behind;  

puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;  
then fill the vaginal opening of the patient with cotton, and insert as much as a fistful;  

puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;  
then make the woman stand up and raise her back little by little, and the cotton will move upward until it reaches the vaginal opening, and the bone will return to its place with the cotton.  

et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:  
And when she wishes to urinate, remove the cotton, and after she has urinated, replace it, and do this for seven days or so:  

si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;  
the fracture will then be restored, and if you wish, take a sheep’s bladder, tie a pipe to its opening, and insert the entire bladder into the vaginal passage;  

puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:  
then blow forcefully into the pipe until the bladder is inflated inside:  

la nature si revenra li brisure;  
thus the fracture will be corrected in the vaginal passage;  

puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.  
then fill it with cotton, and leave it like this for several days, until it is healed.  

Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;  
And when the wrist bone of a man or a woman is fractured, restore it as we have described for the bone of the hip;  

et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.  
and these fractures are not hidden from one who devotes study and practice to them, and understands my book.  

Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:  
For fractures reveal through various conditions the correct method of restoration:  

enten le donques.  
so understand it then.  

En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;  
For the penis, when it is fractured, take a goose’s throat and insert the penis into it;  

puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.  
then wrap it with cloths around, and leave it for three days or thereabouts, and it will heal quickly.  

de brisure avec plaie  
Of fracture with a wound  

Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.  
It is necessary for one who has a fracture with a wound, especially if it is large, such as in the thigh bone or the humerus or similar, to be bled immediately, as the bleeding we have described indicates.  

Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.  
And if the wound heals, staunch it with vitriol, if you have nothing else, then proceed to set the fracture in that same hour or on that day, if no hot abscess forms.  

Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.  
And if a hot abscess forms, delay the setting until the ninth day, until the abscess subsides, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would cause a harmful condition to develop.  

Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.  
And if the broken bone is visible through the uncovered flesh, you must carefully set it with your hands, with slight extension.  

Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;  
And if the extension is not sufficient to equalize with your hands, adjust it with this iron instrument, which is seven or eight fingers long, and its width matches the size of the wound.  

et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;  
And for this, it is necessary for the physician to have three or four of them, depending on the needs of each fracture treatment.  

et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:  
And it should be round and slightly thick so it does not bend under compression on the limb during your work, and it should be sharp at the front and thick from the middle onward, thus:  

Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;  
And it is called a "palainche," for which the curved head must be placed on the visible end of the bone.  

et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.  
And push it in all at once, until it returns, and it is aligned one against the other.  

Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.  
And if the fracture is delicate and the instrument cannot grip the bone well, you must cut the end of the bone so that the instrument can gain control over it.  

Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;  
And if you cannot bring the bone back as we have said, then cut it with a suitable instrument for this, whether a scalpel or saw, as you are able.  

puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.  
Then clean what remains on the bone of roughness and small splinters.  

Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.  
And when the bone is set, and the patient feels great pain afterward, know that it is not in its natural position.  

Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;  
Then ensure it is in its proper place, then soak a cloth in black styptic wine and apply it carefully, especially if it is in summer.  

Et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;  
And do not apply wax or anything else containing oil to the wound, so that it does not cause decay and corruption to develop.  

puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;  
Then apply splints once you have set the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, trimming the covering all around according to the size of the wound, and take great care that the wound is not compressed along with the fracture.  

et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;  
And many times foolish physicians have done this, and have caused death or sometimes gangrene to come upon the patient.  

et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.  
And let the compression be softer and gentler than for other fractures.  

Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;  
And if the wound is bad or large, and you fear that harmful conditions might arise as we have described, and you find pain in the area, then do not apply splints.  

mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.  
Instead, wrap it around with stiff cloths in place of splints, and tie them.  

Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.  
And when you see after one or two days that the wound is generating pus, remove what you had applied with wine, and apply a healing ointment for wounds, such as tetrapharmacum and similar.  

Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.  
And you must untie the limb twice a day, in the morning and evening, until it is set and healed.  

Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.  
And you must position the limb in such a way that the pus flows downward easily.  

Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.  
And if many days pass, and it cannot heal but continues to produce pus, know that there are small bone fragments, for which you must probe the wound with a tent and remove all these loose pieces that cause this pain.  

Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.  
And if a fistula forms in the area, or another type of corruption, you must treat it as described in the chapter above.  

Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;  
And when the bone is broken and exposed in the limb, such as the thigh bone or the humerus, and others like the large bones, do not extract it, for often death results from this, but leave it until it rots.  

par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;  
By chance, it will fall off by itself after twenty or thirty days, then treat the wound if you can.  

et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.  
And if you cannot, then leave it.  

des brus qui vienent sor la sodure  
Of lumps that appear on the healing site  

Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;  
They often appear after the healing of the fracture, especially near a joint, and the appearance of the limb is unpleasant to behold.  

et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.  
And as a result, the limb might not perform its natural functions.  

Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:  
Take care then, if the lump is fresh:  

si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;  
Apply styptic medicines, such as aloe, frankincense, myrrh, sarcocolla, acacia, and similar substances, either one of them or all together, and mix them with styptic wine, egg white, or vinegar.  

et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;  
Apply them to the lump with a cloth, bind it tightly, and do not loosen it for several days.  

et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;  
Then loosen it and reapply the treatment until the lump is removed.  

ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;  
Or press a well-made piece of lead onto it.  

car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;  
For the property of lead is such that it removes all swellings on the limbs.  

et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;  
And if the lump has already hardened like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, cut into it and open the visible excess.  

ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.  
Or shave it with a blade until it is removed, and treat it until it is healed.  

dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison  
Of a limb that is weak after healing  

Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:  
When the fracture of the bone is repaired, and the limb remains weak and delicate afterward, it happens for many reasons:  

de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;  
One is because it was bound too tightly and not properly as it should have been.  

ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;  
Or because there were too many bindings, and nourishment could not reach the limb.  

ou por multitude d’arosement;  
Or due to excessive wetting.  

ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;  
Or from too much movement, and not at the right time.  

ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.  
Or because the body has little blood, thus it is weak.  

Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;  
The treatment is to have the patient eat and strengthen the body until the blood is increased in it.  

et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;  
And give them baths, and provide joy and delight.  

puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;  
Then apply weight to the limb so that it draws much nourishment to it, and frequently bathe it with warm water until nourishment flows to the limb.  

et reviegne a sa figure natureil.  
And it returns to its natural shape.  

dou membre tort aprés la santeit  
Of a limb twisted after healing  

Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:  
When a limb is twisted after repair, and the broken bone is visible, and the shape of the limb is ugly, yet it does not lose its natural function:  

si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;  
Do not believe fools who say the limb must be broken anew, and many foolish physicians have done this in our land.  

et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;  
This practice is condemned, and great harm, even death, can result from it.  

toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;  
However, if the lumps and twisting are fresh, they should be bathed with warm water or softened with cooked herbs, such as mallow leaves, roots, melilot, and similar things.  

et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;  
And make a softening plaster, such as a well-made diachylon, and take the mucilage of mallow, mix it with chicken fat or sesame oil, and apply it as a plaster.  

ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.  
Or take fat figs and mash them with dung from doves, and similar medicines that reduce hardening.  

Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.  
Sometimes the lump is removed by continuous and prolonged rubbing with moist hands.  

Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.  
And administer movement to the limb every hour.  

Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;  
And if the twisting has aged and hardened like stone, and must be removed with iron, cut it down to the bone with a fine scalpel, carefully.  

et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.  
And apply sutures and care in the treatment.  

Ci encomence li livres des dislocations  
Here begins the book of dislocations  

Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.  
Dislocation is when a joint is displaced from its position, causing the limb to be misshapen, and the patient feels great pain and severe injury.  

Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.  
When dislocation occurs in someone, it must be immediately reset without delay.  

Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;  
For if delayed, the area swells, and it may be reset with difficulty in its place.  

por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:  
Therefore, the joint must not be moved while it is swollen.  

maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;  
Often this causes spasms and other pains.  

toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;  
However, when this happens, bleed the patient, then wait until the hot swelling subsides.  

puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.  
Then bathe the limb with warm water and oil, then gently reset it, and treat each limb as its treatment requires.  

Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.  
And I have arranged the chapters of dislocations from the head to the feet.  

des mandibules  
Of the mandibles  

Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:  
It rarely happens that both mandibles are dislocated, and the dislocation of both occurs in two ways:  

ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;  
either they are slightly displaced from their place and somewhat softened;  

ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.  
or they are completely dislocated and hang downward, with saliva flowing from the mouth as it cannot be held in, and the mouth cannot be closed, encumbering the tongue and speech.  

Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.  
When the dislocation is minor, it often corrects itself spontaneously.  

Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;  
But if it is complete and severe, you must restore it quickly without delay;  

et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;  
and in such a way that an assistant holds the patient’s head while the practitioner inserts the thumb of one hand at the root of the mandible’s dislocation inside the mouth, if the dislocation is on both sides;  

et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;  
and the other fingers of the hand are outside to align it properly;  

et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.  
and instruct the patient to relax the mandibles and move them in all directions.  

Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.  
And the practitioner aligns it until it returns to its place.  

Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;  
If repositioning is difficult, especially if both mandibles are involved, they should be bathed with warm water and oil to make the process easier.  

ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.  
Do not delay in restoring them, as we have said.  

Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;  
Once they are properly restored and the patient’s mouth closes well without difficulty, place damp cloths soaked in a salve of rose oil and wax, then secure it lightly with soft bindings;  

et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;  
and let the patient sleep on their back, with their head supported between two cushions, ensuring it does not move to the right or left, avoiding any effort to chew, and eating only soft foods until the pain subsides and the mandibles are stabilized;  

et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.  
and later, they may eat whatever they wish lightly, but avoid exerting effort to open the mouth for eating or drinking until the mandibles are fully stabilized and healed.  

Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.  
If the two mandibles cannot be properly restored in a timely manner and are not returned to their positions, fever and recurring episodes often arise, along with possible diarrhea or vomiting of pure bile.  

Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;  
When you observe this, know that it is fatal.  

et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.  
Many times, those afflicted die within nine days.  

de la forcelle  
Of the sternum  

Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.  
The sternum cannot dislocate from the ribs where it connects to the chest, but it may occasionally dislocate outward, which is easily felt.  

Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;  
The treatment is for the patient to lie often on their back and extend their arms;  

et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;  
then press the area firmly with your palm, and it will return to its place;  

puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;  
then apply a poultice and a bandage, and tighten it;  

et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;  
and the end near the ribs cannot dislocate;  

se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;  
except slightly, and if it ever dislocates, restore it to its place as we have described;  

puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;  
then apply a poultice and bandage, tighten it, and instruct the patient to rest until they are healed;  

et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.  
and in the same way, the head of the shoulder is restored when it is displaced from its place.  

de la dislocation de l’espaule  
Of the dislocation of the shoulder  

Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:  
Know that the shoulder is dislocated only in three ways:  

de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;  
the first is when it is dislocated downward toward the armpit;  

et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;  
the second is toward the chest;  

et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;  
and sometimes it dislocates upward, which is rare;  

et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;  
it does not dislocate backward because of the shoulder blade, nor inward because of the nerves;  

et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;  
it often dislocates downward toward the armpit, especially in those with little flesh, for in them it comes out quickly;  

a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.  
in those with sufficient flesh, it dislocates with difficulty and returns with difficulty.  

Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.  
Sometimes, due to a blow or fracture, the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, leading one to think it is dislocated.  

Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;  
It is necessary to examine it to be certain;  

et adonques encomence la cure.  
then begin the treatment.  

Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;  
The dislocation is recognized when it is downward toward the armpit, and a distinction can be made between the injured shoulder and the healthy one, with clear differences between them.  

et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;  
You will find a hollow at the head of the shoulder, and under the armpit, when touching the head of the shoulder, it will feel as if it were a bone.  

et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;  
The patient cannot bring their hand to their nose nor make any movements.  

et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;  
Likewise, if it is dislocated upward, it is not hidden, as you can clearly feel it by touch.  

et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.  
This type of dislocation can only be treated by repositioning, especially if it is recent or if the patient is a child.  

Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;  
The method is for the assistant to raise the patient’s arm upward, then place their hands under the armpit and lift the joint forcefully upward into place.  

et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;  
The assistant raises the arm and stretches it upward, then places it back down.  

si venra hastanment.  
It will quickly return to place.  

Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;  
If it does not return as we described after a few days, the patient must be bathed in warm water.  

et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;  
Then administer softening and soothing treatments, such as a decoction of marshmallow, fenugreek, and melilot in water, and apply it.  

puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;  
Then let the patient lie on their back, and place an even woolen pad under the armpit, neither too soft nor too hard. The practitioner then puts their heel on the pad, lifts the head of the shoulder with care, and pulls the patient’s hand.  

et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;  
Another assistant holds the patient’s head to prevent it from moving downward.  

celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:  
The shoulder will return immediately, and if you wish, restore it using this method:  

et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;  
Have a man larger than the patient present.  

et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;  
Let him stand on the patient’s side, place his shoulder under the patient’s armpit, and lift the armpit upward so that the patient hangs in the air.  

et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.  
Another assistant pulls the patient’s hand downward toward the abdomen.  

Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.  
If the patient is too light, attach something heavy to them, and the dislocation will immediately return to place.  

Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:  
The shoulder can also be restored using another method:  

et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;  
Place a long wooden rod into the ground, with its head rounded like a pestle, neither too thick nor too thin.  

puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;  
Place it under the patient, but ensure it is covered with soft cloths, and the patient should be positioned along the length of the rod.  

puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;  
Then stretch their arm downward forcefully, and the joint will quickly return to its place.  

et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:  
and if it does not want to return for all these things that we have said, then do this treatment:  

pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:  
take a stick of two arms in length and four fingers in width, which has a rounded head to enter deeply beneath the armpit, in this manner:  

puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;  
then wrap soft cloths around the head of the stick, so that the stick does not harm the patient, and then place it under the patient’s armpit;  

et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:  
and stretch the arm along the length of the stick, and bind the support to the stick, and the arm at the head of the hand, then place the arm on a rung of a wide ladder, and let the hand extend downward, and let the body hang on the other side:  

li jointure reva ens maintenant.  
the joint will return in place immediately.  

Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.  
And when it is in place, in whatever manner it may be, you must place an equal-sized wool ball under the armpit, then apply the plaster prepared with millstone powder, along with incense and egg white, over the entire shoulder and around it, then bind it appropriately under the armpit, and tie the band over the plaster, and brace the hand against the neck, and let the hand remain thus.  

Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;  
And it is necessary for them to eat little, so that the limb is strengthened, for it will heal faster;  

et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve;  
and then they may eat more after five or seven days, and move it;  

et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.  
and if it is firm and not softened, then it is healed.  

Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.  
And if the joint is out of place because of moisture that has come there, or for another reason, then you must apply cauterization in three spots, as is set out earlier in the chapter on cauterization.  

Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis;  
And if you do all this, and it comes undone after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and they cannot raise their arm upward, then know that the nerves at the head of the shoulder are severed, stretched, or softened;  

et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.  
and know that the joint will never again be fixed in its place.  

Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure;  
The dislocation that is toward the chest, the breasts, or behind, is corrected by pressure and stretching of the hands, and it is treated in another manner;  

et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.  
and treat it until it is healed.  

Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.  
And if, after healing, stiffness comes to the limb, and slowness in movement, let the patient bathe many times, until that stiffness is relieved, and it returns to its original condition.  

de la dislocation dou coute  
of the dislocation of the elbow  

Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient;  
Know that the elbow joint is dislocated with difficulty, and with difficulty it returns;  

et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien;  
and if it is dislocated in all directions, and especially in the front and back, the dislocation is not hidden, for it is clearly seen and felt;  

et desalue selonc chescune figure.  
and dislocated according to its particular form.  

Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.  
And when you place the dislocated elbow with the healthy one, you can see it clearly.  

Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.  
For the joint is crooked, and they cannot bend their arm, nor touch their shoulder with it.  

Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener;  
And it is necessary that you set it before warm abscesses appear there, for if warm abscesses come there, it would be difficult to set it;  

et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier;  
and perhaps it cannot be completely reset, especially when it is toward the back;  

si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.  
this is worse than other dislocations, and is of greater pain, and perhaps it brings death.  

Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains;  
And the restoration is, when it is such that it can be reset, that you extend their hand with your two hands;  

et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.  
and their arms are stretched, and the physician’s hands surround the elbow, above and below, and press the joint with their thumbs together, or at the base of their palm, until it returns to its place.  

Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.  
And if the dislocation is in the front, it will return when they press their hand against their other hand and strike the dislocated elbow with the base of the palm.  

Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension;  
And if it does not want to return to its place, then apply strong extension;  

et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension;  
and this is done by two assistants extending the arm while holding it steady so it does not move during the extension;  

puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;  
then turn the arm to each side, after wrapping it in a double cloth, long and wide;  

et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;  
and when the physician has the joint in hand, anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, then press the joint firmly until it returns to place;  

et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.  
and when it is in place, apply a dry plaster with egg white, bind it firmly, hang the arm from the patient’s neck, and leave it for some days, then unbind it.  

Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse;  
And if the joint is firm in its place, then untie the binding and leave it;  

et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis;  
and if you see that the joint does not hold well, reapply the plaster and binding, and leave it for some days until it is firmly set;  

puis le deslie.  
then unbind it.  

Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez;  
And if there is stiffness after the resetting of the joint, and it moves poorly, bathe and gently massage it, and press it until it is relieved;  

ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;  
or place on the joint a fat sheep’s fleece, leave it for one day and one night, then remove it and let it soak in a bath;  

et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain;  
and when it sweats, gently rub the joint, then replace the fleece, and return it to the bath;  

et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez;  
and do this two or three times, until it is healed;  

et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus;  
and if you wish, place cow dung moistened and heated with butter on it, and bind it;  

si revenra a sa disposition.  
and it will return to its proper condition.  

li dislocation de la main  
the dislocation of the hand  

Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures.  
The joint of the hand dislocates, and its resetting is easier than the other joints.  

Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.  
Nevertheless, it must be reset quickly, in the very hour that it is dislocated, before the area swells or a warm abscess appears.  

Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.  
And the resetting is done by placing the dislocated hand on a table, having an assistant stretch the hand, while the physician aligns it, placing their palm on the visible part of the joint and pressing until it returns to place.  

Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu;  
Nevertheless, it is necessary to ensure it is well in place;  

adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.  
then the patient places the back of their hand on a table for extension and resetting.  

Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.  
And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, the patient places the back of their hand on the table, and the physician places their hand on the visible part of the joint.  

S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.  
If it returns immediately, that is good.  

Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.  
If not, apply plasters that soothe warm abscesses, and leave it like that without restarting the treatment.  

Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;  
And if they cannot endure it, and you cannot reset it after some days, the joint will remain twisted;  

et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout:  
and it does not harm the patient except that the hand remains weakened and cannot grip anything firmly:  

adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere;  
then know that the nerves are severed, or the arteries;  

si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.  
and there is no other remedy except cauterization near the affected area, and perhaps nothing else will help.  

Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.  
And when the hand is in place, apply the plaster we mentioned, then bind it and leave it for five days, then unbind it and leave it thus.  

Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.  
And if they cannot move it well and there is some stiffness, soak it in warm water, and rub it until it is healed.  

de la dislocation des dois de la main  
Of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand  

Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;  
Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated to either side, sometimes toward the back of the palm or the front.  

adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;
